## User (2026-04-20 18:28:35)

Your task:  "positive-kernel / repeated-source monotonicity route at the source level"

We are trying to prove the Riemann Hypothesis. Please see attached paper draft.

Current status, in one paragraph:

On the **nonmixed (4)-point side**, the local derivative-geometry story is essentially finished. Exact nonmixed contacts force zeros of (\mathcal R); one-sign (\mathcal R)-intervals are sterile; recurrent exact contacts force affine-planar collapse; isolated zeros of (\mathcal R) are classified by parity; and the repeated-source / first-loss mechanism is now fully reduced: first loss occurs **iff** one diagonally approaches an odd zero of (\mathcal R). So there is no separate first-loss obstruction left beyond odd-zero birth. Equivalently, on a nonmixed arc the whole burden is to exclude odd zeros of the source-level Wronskian
[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'.
]
At the same time, two no-go results are now clear: the current (3)-point package for the original planar curve ((x,S)) does **not** by itself contradict the sheared repeated-node tangent-contact event, and the current source-level ratio/Wronskian/(4\times4)-Wronskian package is still formally too free. So the missing ingredient is now a genuine **source-coupling / shear-transfer theorem**, not more local parity analysis. The repeated-source lane is closed cleanly by the theorem that first loss is exactly diagonal odd-zero birth.

Your task:  "positive-kernel / repeated-source monotonicity route at the source level"

Read the latest draft and work only on the repeated-source / monotonicity formulation. The key objects are:
[
\Gamma_a(x)=
\frac{Y(x)-Y(a)-Y'(a)(x-a)}
{S(x)-S(a)-S'(a)(x-a)},
\qquad
\Psi_a(h)=\frac{D_{u_5}(a,h)}{D_\lambda(a,h)},
]
and the determinant (\mathfrak D(a,h)) controlling the source-level derivative. The repeated-source lane is now fully classified locally: first loss occurs iff one diagonally approaches an odd zero of (\mathcal R). So there is no separate first-loss mechanism left. What remains is to show that on a **genuine opened nonmixed arc**, the needed first odd zero / monotonicity loss cannot occur.

Your task is to push the **positive-kernel / source-determinant** route as far as possible. I want one of the following:

* a one-sign theorem for (\Gamma_a'), (\Psi_a'), or (\mathfrak D(a,h)) near the diagonal on opened nonmixed arcs;
* a theorem that the first odd zero of (\mathcal R) would force a forbidden sign change or variation property for the family (\Gamma_a) or (\Psi_a);
* or a reduction of odd-zero birth to a concrete sign contradiction for (\mathfrak D(a,h)).

Please assume the theorem that repeated-source first loss is exactly diagonal odd-zero birth, and do **not** spend time reproving that classification. The goal here is not local birth theory, but a **global monotonicity / sign exclusion** for the realized family (\Gamma_a), (\Psi_a), or (\mathfrak D(a,h)) on genuine opened nonmixed arcs.

_Thought for 10m 10s_

I think there is a real theorem available here.

The strongest thing I can get from the current kernel machinery is not a full one-sign theorem for \(\Gamma_a'\) or \(\mathfrak D\) on all opened nonmixed arcs, but a sharper obstruction:

> **a segment that sees only one sign change of \(\mathcal R\) cannot support the rigidified first-loss event.**

That is exactly the positive-kernel/source-determinant route, pushed one step beyond what is already in the draft.

---

### 1. The missing companion identity

You already have
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)
=
\frac{1}{B_a(x)^2}\int_a^x \Omega_{a,x}(r)\,\mathcal R(r)\,dr,
\]
and in the normalized nonmixed chart
\[
D_a'(t)=2\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,\mathcal R(a+s(t-a))\,ds.
\]

What is missing, but follows just as easily, is the analogous formula for the **height defect**
\[
\Gamma_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a).
\]

In the normalized nonmixed chart (\(S(t)=t^2\), \(\Gamma_a=D_a\)),
\[
D_a(t)=\int_0^1 (1-s)\,\widetilde Y''(a+s(t-a))\,ds,
\qquad
D_a(a)=\mathcal Z(a),
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
D_a(t)-D_a(a)
=
(t-a)\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,\mathcal R(a+s(t-a))\,ds.
}
\]

Equivalently, in invariant form,
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)
=
\frac{1}{B_a(x)}
\int_a^x \Theta_{a,x}(r)\,\mathcal R(r)\,dr,
}
\]
where
\[
\Theta_{a,x}(r):=\int_r^x (x-t)\,S''(t)\,dt.
\]
On a nonmixed arc, \(\Theta_{a,x}(r)\) has fixed sign after orienting \(x\).

So the rigidified first-loss condition is not one moment equation but **two**:
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_a(x)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]

In normalized segment coordinates \(s\in[0,1]\), these become
\[
\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_{a,x}(s)\,ds=0,
\qquad
\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_{a,x}(s)\,ds=0,
\]
with
\[
R_{a,x}(s):=\mathcal R(a+s(x-a)).
\]

---

### 2. The actual theorem

Let
\[
k_1(s):=s(1-s),\qquad k_0(s):=(1-s)^2.
\]
Then
\[
\frac{k_0(s)}{k_1(s)}=\frac{1-s}{s},
\]
which is strictly decreasing on \((0,1)\).

That gives:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Single-sign-change extremum theorem.}
}
\]

Assume \(a<x\) lie on an opened nonmixed arc, and assume that
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)=0.
\]
Suppose moreover that \(\mathcal R\) has exactly one sign change on \((a,x)\).

Then
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(\Gamma_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
\]
is forced: it equals the sign of \(\mathcal R\) on the **initial side** of the interval \((a,x)\). In particular,
\[
\Gamma_a(x)\neq \mathcal Z(a).
\]

So a segment with exactly one sign change of \(\mathcal R\) can produce a repeated-source extremum, but it can **never** satisfy the rigidified first-loss balance.

#### Proof idea
Write \(R_{a,x}(s)=\sigma(s)\rho(s)\) with \(\rho\ge 0\) and \(\sigma\) changing sign exactly once.  
From \(\Gamma_a'(x)=0\),
\[
\int_0^1 k_1(s)\sigma(s)\rho(s)\,ds=0.
\]
Then
\[
\Gamma_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)
\propto
\int_0^1 k_0(s)\sigma(s)\rho(s)\,ds
=
\int_0^1 \frac{k_0}{k_1}(s)\,k_1(s)\sigma(s)\rho(s)\,ds.
\]
Because \(k_0/k_1\) is strictly decreasing, it is larger on the earlier-sign side than on the later-sign side. Once the \(k_1\)-weighted masses balance, the \(k_0\)-weighted integral keeps the sign of the earlier side. Hence it cannot vanish.

---

### 3. What this gives at source level

Since
\[
\Psi_a(h)=\Gamma_{x(a)}(x(h)),
\qquad
\Psi_a'(h)
\sim \mathfrak D(a,h),
\]
the same statement becomes:

> If \(\Psi_a'(h)=0\) and the pulled-back source-level scalar \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) changes sign exactly once on the source segment from \(a\) to \(h\), then
> \[
> \Psi_a(h)-\mathcal Z(a)
> \]
> has a forced nonzero sign. Therefore
> \[
> \Psi_a'(h)=0,\qquad \Psi_a(h)=\mathcal Z(a)
> \]
> cannot occur simultaneously.

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any realized first-loss segment must cross at least two sign changes of }
\mathcal R
\text{ (hence of } \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\text{).}
}
\]

That is the cleanest monotonicity/sign reduction I can get from the current source-determinant framework.

---

### 4. What it does and does not close

What it **does** show:

- a lone first odd zero is not enough to satisfy the full rigidified first-loss balance on any fixed segment;
- the repeated-source obstruction is now at least a **two-sign-change** phenomenon at the kernel level, not a one-sign-change phenomenon.

What it **does not** yet show:

- it does **not** exclude the local derivative-zero branch born at an odd zero;
- so it does **not** by itself kill odd-zero birth.

But it materially tightens the burden:

> the missing source-coupling theorem no longer has to rule out every local odd-zero extremum directly; it is enough to rule out the additional oscillation needed to turn that local extremum mechanism into a genuine first-loss segment.

That is a real reduction.

---

### 5. The crisp proposition to add

Here is the theorem in paper-style math form.

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Single-sign-change source segment cannot realize rigidified first loss]
\label{prop:single-sign-change-cannot-realize-first-loss}
Let $J$ be an opened nonmixed arc, and let $a<x$ in $J$.
After local nonmixed normalization on $[a,x]$, write
\[
R_{a,x}(s):=\mathcal R(a+s(x-a)),
\qquad 0\le s\le 1.
\]
Then
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)
=
2\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_{a,x}(s)\,ds,
\]
and
\[
\Gamma_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)
=
(x-a)\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_{a,x}(s)\,ds.
\]

Assume that $R_{a,x}$ has exactly one sign change on $(0,1)$.
If
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)=0,
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(\Gamma_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
\]
is the sign of $R_{a,x}$ on the initial side of the sign change.
In particular,
\[
\Gamma_a(x)\neq \mathcal Z(a).
\]

Equivalently, no pair $(a,x)$ for which $\mathcal R$ changes sign exactly once
on $(a,x)$ can satisfy simultaneously
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_a(x)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
Hence any rigidified first-loss segment must cross at least two sign changes of
$\mathcal R$.
\end{proposition}
```

And the source-level corollary is:

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Source-level two-sign-change obstruction]
\label{cor:source-level-two-sign-change-obstruction}
Let $a<h$ lie on an opened nonmixed arc in source coordinates.
Assume
\[
\Psi_a'(h)=0.
\]
If the source-level Wronskian
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
\]
changes sign exactly once on the source interval $[a,h]$, then
\[
\Psi_a(h)\neq \mathcal Z(a).
\]
Equivalently, the simultaneous source-level first-loss conditions
\[
\Psi_a'(h)=0,
\qquad
\Psi_a(h)=\mathcal Z(a)
\]
force at least two sign changes of $\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}$ on $[a,h]$.
\end{corollary}
```

This is the best honest push I see from the positive-kernel / source-determinant lane with the current draft.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 18:42:38)

I’m checking whether the kernel route can be pushed from “two sign changes needed” to something actually fatal, or whether the draft’s freedom still leaves a genuine gap.

_Thought for 6m 35s_

Yes — a bit further, and in a way that feels genuinely structural.

The next useful push is to stop looking only at the kernel average
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)\sim \int \Omega_{a,x}\,\mathcal R
\]
and instead package it as a **triple primitive** of \(\mathcal R\) on each normalized nonmixed segment. That gives a stronger “one-sign-change chamber” theorem.

After local nonmixed normalization \(S(t)=t^2\), write \(D_a=\Gamma_a\). Then the draft already gives
\[
D_a'(x)=2\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,\mathcal R(a+s(x-a))\,ds.
\]
From the same calculation one also gets the two endpoint-gap identities
\[
D_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)
=
(x-a)\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,\mathcal R(a+s(x-a))\,ds,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal Z(x)-D_a(x)
=
(x-a)\int_0^1 s^2\,\mathcal R(a+s(x-a))\,ds.
\]

That is already stronger than the earlier moment argument, because now at any critical pair \(D_a'(x)=0\), the three weights
\[
s(1-s),\qquad (1-s)^2,\qquad s^2
\]
can be compared directly.

If \(\mathcal R\) has exactly one sign change on \((a,x)\), then:
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(D_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
=
\text{sign of the initial lobe of }\mathcal R,
\]
while
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(\mathcal Z(x)-D_a(x)\bigr)
=
\text{sign of the terminal lobe of }\mathcal R.
\]

So a one-sign-change critical point does not just fail the rigidified first-loss condition \(D_a(x)=\mathcal Z(a)\). It actually satisfies the stronger endpoint-separation law:

- if \(\mathcal R\) is \(+\) then \(-\) on \((a,x)\), then
  \[
  D_a(x)>\mathcal Z(a)\quad\text{and}\quad D_a(x)>\mathcal Z(x);
  \]
- if \(\mathcal R\) is \(-\) then \(+\), then
  \[
  D_a(x)<\mathcal Z(a)\quad\text{and}\quad D_a(x)<\mathcal Z(x).
  \]

So the critical value lies **strictly outside** the endpoint-curvature interval. That is better than the earlier “not equal to \(\mathcal Z(a)\)” statement.

The really useful reformulation is this:
\[
F_a(x):=\frac{(x-a)^3}{2}\,D_a'(x)
      =\int_a^x (r-a)(x-r)\,\mathcal R(r)\,dr.
\]
Then
\[
F_a'(x)=\int_a^x (r-a)\,\mathcal R(r)\,dr,
\qquad
F_a''(x)=\int_a^x \mathcal R(r)\,dr=\mathcal Z(x)-\mathcal Z(a),
\qquad
F_a'''(x)=\mathcal R(x).
\]

That is the key extra step.

Because \(F_a'''\) is just \(\mathcal R\), if \(\mathcal R\) has exactly one sign change on a chamber, then \(F_a''\) is unimodal, \(F_a'\) has at most one turning point, and \(F_a\) has at most one positive zero. So for fixed \(a\):

> on any interval where the segment \([a,x]\) sees exactly one sign change of \(\mathcal R\), the equation \(D_a'(x)=0\) has at most one solution.

And that zero, if it exists, is simple. Indeed, at \(D_a'(x)=0\),
\[
F_a'(x)=(x-a)\bigl(\mathcal Z(x)-D_a(x)\bigr),
\]
so by the endpoint-separation law it has the sign of the terminal lobe of \(\mathcal R\), hence is nonzero.

This gives a clean geometric picture of the repeated-source branch in a one-sign-change chamber:

- for each anchor \(a\), there is at most one target \(x\) with \(D_a'(x)=0\);
- the zero is transverse;
- the critical branch is harmless there in the sense that it cannot satisfy the rigidified first-loss equality \(D_a(x)=\mathcal Z(a)\);
- so a locally born odd-zero branch cannot produce genuine first-loss behavior until the segment picks up a **second** sign change of \(\mathcal R\).

That last sentence is probably the best honest “further push” from this route:

> **odd-zero birth is not enough; to participate in actual monotonicity loss, the born critical branch must survive until a second sign change of \(\mathcal R\) appears on the segment.**

At source level this translates directly through
\[
\Psi_a(h)=\Gamma_{x(a)}(x(h)),
\qquad
\mathfrak D(a,h)\sim D_{x(a)}'(x(h)).
\]
So on a source interval where \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) has exactly one sign change, for each source anchor \(a\) there is at most one \(h\) with \(\mathfrak D(a,h)=0\), that zero is simple, and it cannot realize the rigidified first-loss balance. Any genuine nonmixed obstruction must therefore span at least **two** sign changes of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\).

I do not think the positive-kernel route alone gets all the way to contradiction from here. But it does sharpen the burden substantially. The remaining theorem is no longer “kill odd-zero birth.” It is:

> show that on a genuine opened nonmixed arc, the source-level Wronskian cannot supply the **second oscillation** needed to turn a locally born repeated-source critical branch into an actual first-loss mechanism.

That feels like a real reduction, not just repackaging.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 18:51:08)

_Thought for 8m 40s_

Yes. I think the next real step is a **transport theorem for the born critical branch**. It pushes the positive-kernel route further than the earlier “two sign changes are needed” statement.

Work in the normalized nonmixed chart, so \(S(t)=t^2\), \(\mathcal Z=\frac12\widetilde Y''\), \(\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'\), and
\[
D_a(t)=\frac{\widetilde Y(t)-\widetilde Y(a)-\widetilde Y'(a)(t-a)}{(t-a)^2}.
\]
Then
\[
D_a'(t)=2\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,\mathcal R(a+s(t-a))\,ds.
\]

Now suppose \(t=\tau(a)\) is a simple local branch of critical points:
\[
D_a'(\tau(a))=0,\qquad a<\tau(a).
\]
Define the critical value
\[
V(a):=D_a(\tau(a)).
\]

The useful new fact is that this branch satisfies an exact transport system.

First,
\[
\partial_a D_a(t)=\frac{2}{t-a}\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
\]
This is just differentiation of the divided difference. So along the critical branch,
\[
\boxed{
V'(a)=\frac{2}{\tau(a)-a}\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
}
\]

Second, using the first-loss rigidification identities already in the draft, in the normalized chart one gets
\[
\partial_a M(a,t)=2(t-a)^2(\mathcal Z(a)-D_a(t)),
\qquad
\partial_t M(a,t)=2(t-a)^2(\mathcal Z(t)-D_a(t))
\]
at points where \(M(a,t)=0\), and since \(M(a,\tau(a))=0\),
\[
0=\frac{d}{da}M(a,\tau(a))
=\partial_a M+\partial_t M\,\tau'(a).
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\tau'(a)=\frac{V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)}.
}
\]

Those two formulas are the right “branch dynamics” equations.

Now combine them with the kernel identities. At a critical pair \(t=\tau(a)\), set \(L=\tau(a)-a\) and \(R_{a,\tau}(s)=\mathcal R(a+sL)\). Then
\[
0=D_a'(\tau(a))=2\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_{a,\tau}(s)\,ds,
\]
and
\[
V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)
=
L\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_{a,\tau}(s)\,ds.
\]
Also, because the middle weight vanishes at a critical pair,
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)
=
L\int_0^1 s^2\,R_{a,\tau}(s)\,ds.
\]

So if the segment \([a,\tau(a)]\) sees exactly one sign change of \(\mathcal R\), then the earlier monotone-ratio argument applies twice:

- \((1-s)^2/(s(1-s))=(1-s)/s\) is strictly decreasing, so
  \[
  \operatorname{sgn}\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
  \]
  is the sign of the initial lobe of \(\mathcal R\);

- \(s^2/(s(1-s))=s/(1-s)\) is strictly increasing, so
  \[
  \operatorname{sgn}\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr)
  \]
  is the sign of the terminal lobe.

Since those lobes have opposite signs, one gets
\[
\boxed{
\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr)<0,
\qquad
\tau'(a)<0.
}
\]

That gives a much sharper statement than before:

> On any chamber where the critical segment sees exactly one sign change of \(\mathcal R\), the born critical branch has strictly negative slope, stays simple, and its critical value lies strictly outside the endpoint-curvature interval \([\mathcal Z(a),\mathcal Z(\tau(a))]\).

In particular,
\[
V(a)\neq \mathcal Z(a),\qquad V(a)\neq \mathcal Z(\tau(a)),
\]
so the branch cannot hit the rigidified first-loss condition there. Equally important, since \(\tau'(a)\neq 0\), the branch cannot flatten there.

That is the clean “no-return in the one-sign-change chamber” theorem.

The next structural consequence is this.

Take the odd-zero birth branch coming from an isolated odd zero \(b\) of \(\mathcal R\). Let \(I\) be the maximal interval of continuation on which every segment \([a,\tau(a)]\) contains exactly that one sign change. On \(I\), the branch is analytic, simple, and \(\tau'(a)<0\). So the only way it can ever leave that chamber is if the sign-change count of \(\mathcal R\) on \([a,\tau(a)]\) changes. For an analytic fixed \(\mathcal R\), that can only happen when a zero of \(\mathcal R\) crosses an endpoint of the segment. Since the branch stays simple inside the chamber, there is no internal catastrophe available before that.

So you get:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any global obstruction branch issued from an odd zero }b
\text{ must continue until one endpoint hits a second zero }c\neq b\text{ of }\mathcal R.
}
\]

Equivalently, at source level:

- let \(h=\sigma(a)\) be a simple branch of solutions of
  \[
  \mathfrak D(a,h)=0,
  \]
  equivalently \(\Psi_a'(h)=0\);
- on the chamber where the source segment \([a,h]\) sees exactly one sign change of
  \[
  \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},
  \]
  the branch has strictly negative slope in the induced \(x\)-coordinate and cannot satisfy
  \[
  \Psi_a(h)=\mathcal Z(a);
  \]
- therefore any genuine nonmixed obstruction branch must connect one odd zero of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) to a second zero of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\).

That is the strongest honest push I can get from the positive-kernel/source-determinant route alone.

What I do **not** see from the current draft is a way to rule out that second-zero connection purely by generic kernel algebra. The present machinery seems to reduce the problem to a very concrete target:

> prove that on a genuine opened nonmixed arc, the \(\mathfrak D=0\) branch born at an odd zero of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) cannot continue all the way to a second zero of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\).

So the attack has sharpened. The remaining theorem is no longer “exclude odd-zero birth” and not even just “need two sign changes.” It is:

> **zero-connection exclusion for the source-level Wronskian branch**.

That feels like the right next theorem to try to prove.

If you want, I’ll turn this into exact LaTeX insertions: a proposition for the critical-branch transport system, a corollary giving the negative-slope/no-return chamber, and a remark stating the zero-connection reduction.

_Thought for 4m 17s_

Yes. Here are the exact insertions I would make.

The main new block should go **immediately after** `Corollary~\ref{cor:source-level-two-sign-change-obstruction}` and **before** `\begin{remark}[What remains on the nonmixed $4$-point side]`.

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Transport equations for a repeated-source critical branch]
\label{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}
Let $J$ be an opened nonmixed arc, and work in a local normalized nonmixed
chart on which
\[
S(t)=t^2,
\qquad
\Gamma_a=D_a.
\]
Let $U\subset J$ be an interval, and let
\[
\tau:U\to J
\]
be a real-analytic function such that
\[
\tau(a)>a,
\qquad
D_a'(\tau(a))=0
\qquad (a\in U).
\]
Set
\[
V(a):=D_a(\tau(a)).
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
V'(a)=\frac{2}{\tau(a)-a}\,\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
\]

\item
\[
D_a''(\tau(a))
=
\frac{2}{(\tau(a)-a)^2}\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr).
\]

\item
At any point $a\in U$ where $D_a''(\tau(a))\neq 0$,
\[
\tau'(a)
=
\frac{V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)}
{\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write
\[
D_a(t)
=
\frac{\widetilde Y(t)-\widetilde Y(a)-\widetilde Y'(a)(t-a)}{(t-a)^2}.
\]
Differentiating in $a$ gives
\[
\partial_a D_a(t)
=
\frac{2}{t-a}\,\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
\]
Evaluating at $t=\tau(a)$ and using $D_a'(\tau(a))=0$ yields
\[
V'(a)
=
\frac{d}{da}D_a(\tau(a))
=
\partial_a D_a(\tau(a))
=
\frac{2}{\tau(a)-a}\,\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr),
\]
which proves (1).

Now use the rigidification scalar
\[
M(a,t):=B_a(t)^2\,\Gamma_a'(t).
\]
In the normalized chart,
\[
B_a(t)=(t-a)^2,
\qquad
\Gamma_a=D_a,
\qquad
M(a,t)=(t-a)^4\,D_a'(t).
\]
By Remark~\ref{rem:first-loss-rigidification-nonmixed},
\[
\partial_t M(a,t)
=
2(t-a)^2\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(t)-D_a(t)\bigr).
\]
At $t=\tau(a)$ we have $D_a'(\tau(a))=0$, so
\[
\partial_t M(a,\tau(a))
=
(\tau(a)-a)^4\,D_a''(\tau(a)).
\]
Comparing the two formulas gives
\[
(\tau(a)-a)^4\,D_a''(\tau(a))
=
2(\tau(a)-a)^2\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr),
\]
hence (2).

Finally, still by Remark~\ref{rem:first-loss-rigidification-nonmixed},
at points where $M(a,t)=0$ one has
\[
\partial_a M(a,t)
=
2(t-a)^2\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(a)-D_a(t)\bigr),
\]
in the normalized chart. Since
\[
M(a,\tau(a))=0,
\]
differentiating in $a$ gives
\[
0=\frac{d}{da}M(a,\tau(a))
=
\partial_a M(a,\tau(a))
+
\partial_t M(a,\tau(a))\,\tau'(a).
\]
Substituting the formulas above yields
\[
0
=
2(\tau(a)-a)^2\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(a)-V(a)\bigr)
+
2(\tau(a)-a)^2\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr)\tau'(a).
\]
If $D_a''(\tau(a))\neq 0$, then by (2),
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\neq 0,
\]
so solving for $\tau'(a)$ gives (3).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[One-sign-change chamber is no-return for the born critical branch]
\label{cor:one-sign-change-chamber-no-return}
In the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch},
assume moreover that for every $a\in U$ the segment
\[
[a,\tau(a)]
\]
contains exactly one sign change of $\mathcal R$.

Then for every $a\in U$:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
\]
is the sign of the initial lobe of $\mathcal R$ on $[a,\tau(a)]$;

\item
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr)
\]
is the sign of the terminal lobe of $\mathcal R$ on $[a,\tau(a)]$;

\item
\[
\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr)<0;
\]

\item
\[
D_a''(\tau(a))\neq 0,
\qquad
\tau'(a)<0;
\]

\item
\[
V(a)\notin [\,\mathcal Z(a),\mathcal Z(\tau(a))\,].
\]
In particular,
\[
V(a)\neq \mathcal Z(a),
\]
so the branch cannot realize the rigidified first-loss condition anywhere on
$U$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The first sign statement is exactly
Proposition~\ref{prop:single-sign-change-cannot-realize-first-loss} applied to
the critical pair $(a,\tau(a))$.

For the second sign statement, write
\[
R_{a,\tau(a)}(s):=\mathcal R(a+s(\tau(a)-a)).
\]
Since
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a)
=
(\tau(a)-a)\int_0^1 R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds
\]
and
\[
V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)
=
(\tau(a)-a)\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds,
\]
one gets
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)
=
(\tau(a)-a)\int_0^1 (2s-s^2)\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds.
\]
At the critical pair,
\[
0=D_a'(\tau(a))
=
2\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds,
\]
so
\[
\int_0^1 (2s-s^2)\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds
=
\int_0^1 s^2\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds.
\]
Hence
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)
=
(\tau(a)-a)\int_0^1 s^2\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds.
\]
Now set
\[
k_1(s):=s(1-s),
\qquad
k_2(s):=s^2.
\]
Then
\[
\frac{k_2(s)}{k_1(s)}=\frac{s}{1-s}
\]
is strictly increasing on $(0,1)$. Repeating the weighted signed-mass argument
from the proof of
Proposition~\ref{prop:single-sign-change-cannot-realize-first-loss} shows that
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr)
\]
is the sign of the terminal lobe of $\mathcal R$.

The two signs are therefore opposite, which proves (3). Then
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(2)
gives
\[
D_a''(\tau(a))\neq 0,
\]
and
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(3)
gives
\[
\tau'(a)<0.
\]
Finally, opposite signs of
\[
V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)
\]
mean exactly that $V(a)$ lies strictly outside the endpoint-curvature interval
\[
[\,\mathcal Z(a),\mathcal Z(\tau(a))\,].
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Zero-connection reduction for the repeated-source branch]
\label{rem:zero-connection-reduction-repeated-source}
Let $b$ be an isolated odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$, and let
\[
t=\tau(a)
\]
denote the local born repeated-source critical branch supplied by
Proposition~\ref{prop:parity-classification-isolated-nonmixed-R-zeros}.
On any maximal continuation interval on which each segment
\[
[a,\tau(a)]
\]
contains exactly one sign change of $\mathcal R$,
Corollary~\ref{cor:one-sign-change-chamber-no-return} shows that the branch
remains simple, satisfies
\[
\tau'(a)<0,
\]
and cannot realize the rigidified first-loss condition
\[
D_a(\tau(a))=\mathcal Z(a).
\]

Thus the only internal way for such a branch to leave the one-sign-change
chamber is for the sign-change count on the segment to change; for analytic
$\mathcal R$, this occurs only when an endpoint of the segment meets another
zero of $\mathcal R$ (equivalently, unless the branch exits the local chart or
the opened arc). Via
Remark~\ref{rem:source-determinant-reformulation-Gammaa},
the same statement holds at source level for a local branch of
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0.
\]
Accordingly, any genuine repeated-source obstruction branch must either leave
the nonmixed chart/arc or connect one odd zero of
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
\]
to a second zero of $\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}$.
\end{remark}
```

Then I would make one replacement inside `Remark~\ref{rem:what-remains-nonmixed-after-R-zero-bridge}`.

Replace this paragraph:

```latex
Accordingly, the genuinely live nonmixed $4$-point burden is no longer local
birth, nor repeated-source first loss, nor generic determinant sign.  It is the
source-coupling problem of excluding odd zeros of
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},
\]
equivalently of $\mathcal R$, on genuine opened nonmixed arcs. Any stronger
formulation involving $\Gamma_a$, $\Psi_a$, or $\mathfrak D(a,h)$ should
now be regarded as a source-level route to that same odd-zero exclusion
problem, not as an additional independent bottleneck.
```

with:

```latex

birth, nor repeated-source first loss, nor generic determinant sign.  The

segment sees exactly one sign change of $\mathcal R$, the born critical branch
is simple, has strictly negative slope, and cannot realize the rigidified
first-loss condition
\[
\Gamma_a(x)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
Equivalently, at source level, a local branch of
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\]
cannot become a genuine obstruction until the source segment acquires a second
zero of
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}.
\]
So the sharpened remaining nonmixed burden is a source-coupling / zero-connection
exclusion theorem for odd zeros of
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},
\]
equivalently of $\mathcal R$, on genuine opened nonmixed arcs.
```

## User (2026-04-20 19:15:09)

## Assistant (2026-04-20 19:19:34)

_Thought for 4m 22s_

Yes. There is at least one more genuine reduction on this line, and one important sharpening.

The sharpening is this: everywhere we’ve been saying “second zero,” the right phrase is really **second sign-changing zero**, i.e. **second odd zero** of \(\mathcal R\) (equivalently of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\)). An even zero does not change the sign-change count on the segment, so it does not break the one-sign-change chamber.

That lets you push the current line one step further.

The clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{\text{If an opened nonmixed arc contains at most one odd zero of }\mathcal R,
\text{ then repeated-source first loss is impossible on that arc.}}
\]

Why this is true:

- if there is no odd zero, there is no birth mechanism at all;
- if there is one odd zero \(b\), any born repeated-source critical branch stays in the one-sign-change chamber for as long as the segment remains in the arc, because no second odd zero can enter the segment;
- on that chamber, your new transport/no-return theorem applies: the branch is simple, has \(\tau'(a)<0\), and cannot satisfy the rigidified first-loss equality.

So the remaining nonmixed repeated-source problem is not “exclude odd zeros on opened arcs” in full generality anymore. It is narrower:

\[
\boxed{\text{exclude a branch connecting one odd zero of }\mathcal R
\text{ to a second odd zero of }\mathcal R.}
\]

And you can sharpen that again.

Order the odd zeros on the arc by position:
\[
b_1<b_2<\cdots<b_m.
\]
Then any genuine obstruction branch can only involve **adjacent odd zeros in this order**. It cannot skip an odd zero, because the first time the one-sign-change chamber can fail is exactly when the segment first picks up another sign change, and that first extra sign change comes from the nearest odd zero on the expanding side.

So the line of attack reduces all the way to a **nearest-neighbor odd-zero connection problem**.

That is a real improvement. It means the minimal bad configuration is no longer some vague global oscillation of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\); it is this:

> there exist two adjacent odd zeros \(b<c\) of \(\mathcal R\) on a genuine opened nonmixed arc, and a repeated-source critical branch born at \(b\) survives all the way until the segment first reaches \(c\).

That is the first configuration not already excluded by the current kernel/transport machinery.

I would formulate the next theorem target exactly that way:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Adjacent-odd-zero exclusion.}\quad
\text{A born repeated-source critical branch cannot continue from one odd zero}
\\
\text{of }\mathcal R\text{ to the next odd zero on a genuine opened nonmixed arc.}
}
\]

That is now the right bottleneck for this line.

There is also a modest draft correction I would make if you insert the current remarks: change “second zero” to “second odd zero” or “second sign-changing zero” in the zero-connection remark. That makes the reduction sharper and more correct.

If you want, I can give you the exact LaTeX insertions for:

- the “at most one odd zero implies sterility” proposition,
- the “adjacent odd zero reduction” corollary,
- and the wording fixes replacing “second zero” by “second odd zero / sign-changing zero.”

## 2) Insert this new proposition + remark immediately after that remark and before `\begin{remark}[What remains on the nonmixed $4$-point side]`

```latex
\begin{proposition}[At most one odd zero implies no genuine repeated-source obstruction]
\label{prop:at-most-one-odd-zero-no-genuine-repeated-source-obstruction}
Let $J$ be an opened nonmixed arc. Assume that $\mathcal R$ has at most one
odd-order zero on $J$. Then there is no pair $a<x$ in $J$ such that
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_a(x)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
Equivalently, there is no source-level pair $a<h$ on the corresponding source
arc such that
\[
\Psi_a'(h)=0,
\qquad
\Psi_a(h)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
On a nonmixed arc, $\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}$ differs from $\mathcal R$ only
by a nonvanishing analytic factor
(Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point}), so odd
zeros and sign changes of the two objects coincide.

If $\mathcal R$ has at most one odd-order zero on $J$, then every segment
contained in $J$ contains at most one sign change of $\mathcal R$ (equivalently
of $\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}$), since even-order zeros do not change sign.
Hence Corollary~\ref{cor:source-level-two-sign-change-obstruction} excludes any
simultaneous source-level solution of
\[
\Psi_a'(h)=0,
\qquad
\Psi_a(h)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
Via Remark~\ref{rem:source-determinant-reformulation-Gammaa}, this is
equivalent to the planar formulation
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_a(x)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Minimal unresolved configuration on this route]
\label{rem:minimal-unresolved-configuration-repeated-source}
Proposition~\ref{prop:at-most-one-odd-zero-no-genuine-repeated-source-obstruction}
shows that the positive-kernel / source-determinant route has already ruled out
every opened nonmixed arc carrying at most one odd zero of $\mathcal R}$.
Accordingly, the first unresolved configuration on this route is no longer a
single odd-zero birth, but an arc carrying at least two odd zeros of
$\mathcal R$.

In particular, the minimal genuinely live scenario is a repeated-source
critical branch born at one odd zero of $\mathcal R$ and continuing until the
segment acquires the next odd zero. Thus the sharpened source-coupling target
is an adjacent-odd-zero connection exclusion theorem on genuine opened
nonmixed arcs.
\end{remark}
```

There is one tiny typo to fix in that remark after you paste it:

```latex
at most one odd zero of $\mathcal R}$.
```
to
```latex
at most one odd zero of $\mathcal R$.
```

So the final pasted version of that sentence should read:

```latex

shows that the positive-kernel / source-determinant route has already ruled out
every opened nonmixed arc carrying at most one odd zero of $\mathcal R$.
```

## User (2026-04-20 19:30:02)

## Assistant (2026-04-20 19:30:21)

_Thought for 18s_

I would say: **basically done as a free-standing branch, but not fully dead**.

More precisely, I think the current positive-kernel / monotonicity route has been pushed to its natural frontier. It has already given the useful reductions:

- first loss is not a separate mechanism;
- one-sign-change chambers are sterile for genuine first loss;
- any genuine obstruction needs at least two **odd** zeros;
- the minimal live picture is an **odd-zero connection** problem.

That is a real endpoint. I do **not** think more grinding on the same kernel averages, by themselves, is likely to suddenly produce a contradiction.

So my honest assessment is:

**As a broad exploratory lane: yes, mostly exhausted.**  
**As a sharply targeted theorem: there is still one live attack left.**

That live target is:

\[
\boxed{\text{adjacent odd-zero connection exclusion}}
\]

Namely: prove that a repeated-source critical branch born at one odd zero of \(\mathcal R\) cannot continue all the way until the segment first reaches the next odd zero.

That is the one remaining theorem on this line that would actually move the proof.

If you want to keep attacking this branch, I would only do it in one of these very specific ways:

First, a **minimal bad pair** argument. Assume a counterexample and choose the first anchor \(a\) for which the born branch reaches a second odd zero. Then try to derive a contradiction from first-contact geometry at that endpoint. This is the cleanest remaining attack within the present framework.

Second, a **branch transport plus endpoint asymptotics** attack. Use the formulas for \(V'(a)\) and \(\tau'(a)\), and study what must happen as the moving endpoint approaches the second odd zero. If one can show the required limiting behavior of \(V(a)\) is incompatible with the local odd-zero model at the target endpoint, that would close the branch.

Third, a **new structural input** at source level: some total-positivity, variation-diminishing, or Sturm/Chebyshev-type fact for the realized family. Without something like that, I doubt the current kernel identities alone will kill the two-odd-zero connection.

So my recommendation would be:

- treat this branch as **reduced to one precise bottleneck**;
- stop broad exploration here;
- either attack the **adjacent odd-zero connection theorem** directly,
- or switch effort to the more global **source-coupling / shear-transfer** route, which feels likelier to supply the missing structure.

If you want, I can now write a clean handoff paragraph describing exactly where this branch stands and the single remaining theorem it needs.
## User (2026-04-20 19:42:14)

## Assistant (2026-04-20 19:42:18)

I’m reading the actual source-coupling and shear-transfer sections now rather than extrapolating from prior reductions, so I can tell you whether the draft already contains a hidden closure or just a sharper handoff.

_Thought for 3m 1s_

Holistically: **no, the draft does not yet solve the two-odd-zero issue**.

But it **does** isolate it very sharply, and it points to a fairly specific next direction.

What the draft now says, taken together, is:

The current **generic source-level algebra** is not enough.  
That is exactly what `Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-package-not-enough}` says: the ratio/Wronskian/\(4\times4\)-Wronskian package is still formally too free.

The current **fixed-level sheared route** is not enough.  
That is what `Remark~\ref{rem:no-go-fixed-level-chamber-exit-route}` says: even when a fixed shear level \(\gamma\) has two nearby curvature zeros, the sheared opposite-side branch can run to the second zero by boundary exit with no interior common-tangent contradiction.

The current **local moving-shear route near one odd zero** is also not enough.  
That is what `Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}` and `Remark~\ref{rem:ceiling-local-shear-transfer-route}` say: on the actual born repeated-source branch, the rooted numerator
\[
D_{f_a}(a,h),\qquad f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\]
has a fixed nonzero signed defect near the odd zero. So local odd-zero birth does **not** already transfer to the rooted sheared event.

Those three points together mean the draft has **not** closed the adjacent/two-odd-zero case. The obstruction really survives there.

What it **has** done is identify the correct shape of the missing theorem:

It cannot be a theorem about frozen \(\gamma\).  
It cannot be a theorem about local odd-zero birth alone.  
It has to be a theorem about the **source-pinned moving shear**
\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda
\]
along the continued critical branch
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
\Psi_a'(h)=0.
\]

That is the real hint in the draft.

There is also one extra structural observation now available from the inserted transport system, and I think it is the best next foothold.

Along a continued critical branch \(t=\tau(a)\), write
\[
V(a):=D_a(\tau(a)),
\qquad
G(a):=V(a)-\mathcal Z(a).
\]
From `Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}` you immediately get
\[
V'(a)=\frac{2}{\tau(a)-a}\,G(a),
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
G'(a)=\frac{2}{\tau(a)-a}\,G(a)-\mathcal R(a).
}
\]

So at any rooted point of the moving-shear defect, meaning \(G(a_*)=0\),
\[
\boxed{
G'(a_*)=-\mathcal R(a_*).
}
\]

And from the same transport formula,
\[
\tau'(a)=\frac{G(a)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)},
\]
so at such a rooted point,
\[
\boxed{
\tau'(a_*)=0
}
\]
provided \(\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq V(a_*)\), which is the generic situation away from collapse.

That is not a contradiction yet, but it is a strong hint:

> **the first rooted point of the moving-shear defect is forced to be a stationary point of the target map \(\tau(a)\), and the crossing of the rooted defect is controlled exactly by the anchor-side sign \(-\mathcal R(a_*)\).**

That suggests the next theorem should be a **first-root / stationary-contact theorem**, not another parity theorem.

Here is how I would phrase the genuine next direction.

At a first rooted point along the born branch, the source-pinned shear theorem says the triple \((c,v_5,f_a)\) has a repeated-node tangent-contact event. By `Remark~\ref{rem:source-level-form-of-shear-transfer}` and `Proposition~\ref{prop:sheared-repeated-node-forces-two-R-zeros}`, this forces at least two interior zeros of
\[
J_{f_a}=(\mathcal Z-\mathcal Z(a))J_\lambda,
\]
equivalently at least two interior points where
\[
\mathcal Z(r)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]

Now combine that with the adjacent-odd-zero picture. Between two adjacent odd zeros of \(\mathcal R\), the derivative \(\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'\) has fixed sign, so \(\mathcal Z\) is monotone there. Therefore the first rooted point cannot happen just by “reaching” the second odd zero. The moving level \(\mathcal Z=\mathcal Z(a)\) has to **reappear on the far side** in the right multiplicity pattern. That is a much tighter configuration than merely “there are two odd zeros.”

So my honest read is:

- **No**, the current source-coupling/shear-transfer package does not solve the two-odd-zero problem.
- **Yes**, it points very clearly to the next direction:
  a theorem about the **first rooted point of**
  \[
  G(a)=\Psi_a(\sigma(a))-\mathcal Z(a),
  \]
  using the moving shear \(f_a\), the stationary condition \(\tau'(a_*)=0\), and the forced level-set geometry
  \[
  \mathcal Z(r)=\mathcal Z(a_*).
  \]

If I were choosing the next attack, I would make it this:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{First-root / adjacent-odd-zero exclusion: }
\text{the born branch } \mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\text{ cannot acquire its first root}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{at a stationary point } \tau'(a_*)=0
\text{ while } J_{f_{a_*}}
\text{ has exactly the adjacent-odd-zero level geometry forced by the arc.}
}
\]

That feels like the real next theorem the draft is asking for.

If you want, I can turn that into exact LaTeX insertions: one short proposition for the ODE of the rooted defect \(G\), and one remark spelling out the “first rooted point = stationary target + moving-level recrossing” reduction.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 19:46:17)

I’m pushing directly on the first-root / stationary-contact bottleneck now: either it turns into a real contradiction with adjacent-odd-zero geometry, or we’ll see exactly what extra theorem is still missing.

_Thought for 9m 9s_

Yes. I can push it one real step further.

The best new object is the **rooted defect along the continued critical branch**
\[
G(a):=\Psi_a(\sigma(a))-\mathcal Z(a),
\]
equivalently in the normalized \(x\)-chart,
\[
G(a)=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a).
\]

This is the quantity that has to hit \(0\) for the moving-shear route to succeed. The transport proposition already in the draft gives an exact ODE for it.

Write
\[
L(a):=\tau(a)-a,\qquad V(a):=D_a(\tau(a)).
\]
Since \(G=V-\mathcal Z\), from
\[
V'(a)=\frac{2}{L(a)}(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a))
\]
one gets immediately
\[
\boxed{
G'(a)=\frac{2}{L(a)}\,G(a)-\mathcal R(a).
}
\]

That is useful. At any first rooted point \(a_*\) with
\[
G(a_*)=0,
\]
one has
\[
\boxed{
G'(a_*)=-\mathcal R(a_*).
}
\]

So unless the anchor itself lands on another zero of \(\mathcal R\), the first rooting is automatically **transverse**. It is not a soft or higher-order disappearance of the local defect. The signed defect crosses linearly, and the direction of crossing is dictated exactly by the anchor-side sign of \(\mathcal R\).

That already sharpens the picture.

Now combine this with
\[
\tau'(a)=\frac{G(a)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)}.
\]
At a rooted point with \(\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq V(a_*)\), i.e.
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq \mathcal Z(a_*),
\]
one gets
\[
\boxed{
\tau'(a_*)=0.
}
\]
Differentiating once more gives
\[
\boxed{
\tau''(a_*)=
-\frac{\mathcal R(a_*)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-\mathcal Z(a_*)}.
}
\]

So the first rooted point is forced to be a **stationary point of the target map** \(a\mapsto \tau(a)\), and generically a strict local extremum.

That is the first strong structural gain.

There is a second one. Define the moving-shear divided difference
\[
F(a,t):=
A_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\,B_a(t)
=
(t-a)^2\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
\]
in the normalized chart \(S(t)=t^2\). At a rooted critical point \((a_*,t_*)\) one has
\[
F(a_*,t_*)=0,
\qquad
\partial_tF(a_*,t_*)=0.
\]
But now the transport identities give more:
\[
\partial_aF(a_*,t_*)
=
-(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*),
\]
and
\[
\partial_{tt}F(a_*,t_*)
=
2\bigl(\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)\bigr).
\]

So whenever \(\mathcal R(a_*)\neq 0\) and \(\mathcal Z(t_*)\neq \mathcal Z(a_*)\), the moving-shear zero set is locally a genuine fold:
\[
\boxed{
a-a_*
=
-\frac{\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)}{(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*)}
\,(t-t_*)^2
+o\!\bigl((t-t_*)^2\bigr).
}
\]

That matters because it tells you exactly what the first rooted point is geometrically: it is not the local odd-zero birth mechanism in disguise. It is a **post-birth fold** of the moving-shear family.

Now bring in the fixed-level sheared theorem. Set
\[
\gamma_*:=\mathcal Z(a_*).
\]
If \(\mathcal R(a_*)\neq 0\), then \(a_*\) is a simple odd zero of
\[
J_{\gamma_*}=(\mathcal Z-\gamma_*)J_\lambda.
\]
So for the fixed shear \(\widetilde Y_{\gamma_*}=Y-\gamma_*S\), the proposition on uniform fixed-level nonrecurrence applies at the odd zero \(a_*\): on its distinguished opposite-side branch inside the maximal slope-overlap block, one has
\[
\partial_t\widetilde H_{3,\gamma_*}\neq 0.
\]

But a rooted point is exactly
\[
\widetilde H_{3,\gamma_*}(a_*,t_*)=0,
\qquad
\partial_t\widetilde H_{3,\gamma_*}(a_*,t_*)=0.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{any nondegenerate first rooted point must lie \emph{beyond} the maximal
fixed-level slope-overlap chamber born at }a_*.
}
\]

That is the key sharpening. It means the first rooted point cannot occur in the clean fixed-level chamber where the sheared branch is controlled by the existing nonrecurrence theorem. It can only occur **after boundary exit** of that fixed-level branch.

So the whole two-odd-zero problem now tightens to this:

- the one-sign-change chamber is sterile;
- the rooted defect \(G\) crosses transversely when it first vanishes;
- the target map \(\tau\) is stationary there;
- and the rooted event must occur only after the fixed-level branch based at the anchor has already left its monotone-slope chamber.

That is a real reduction. It tells you exactly where the missing theorem has to live:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{post-boundary-exit moving-shear exclusion}
}
\]

In other words, the remaining theorem is no longer “exclude odd-zero birth,” and not even just “exclude two odd zeros.” It is:

> show that after the fixed-level branch born at the anchor leaves its slope-overlap chamber, the moving level \(\gamma=\mathcal Z(a)\) still cannot create a first stationary common-tangent point before the adjacent odd-zero connection is completed.

I do not think the current draft proves that yet. But this is now much sharper than before.

The cleanest next proposition to try is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{At any first rooted point }(a_*,\tau(a_*))
\text{ with }\mathcal R(a_*)\neq 0,
\text{ the point }\tau(a_*)
\text{ lies strictly beyond the fixed-level chamber boundary for }
\gamma_*=\mathcal Z(a_*),
}
\]
together with the fold formulas above. Once that is written down, the adjacent-two-odd-zero problem becomes a very concrete post-boundary-exit geometry problem rather than a vague source-coupling gap.

If you want, I’ll turn exactly this into LaTeX insertions for the current draft.

### 1) Insert this block there

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Rooted-defect transport and stationary first root]
\label{prop:rooted-defect-transport-stationary-first-root}
In the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch},
define
\[
L(a):=\tau(a)-a,
\qquad
G(a):=V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a).
\]
Then
\[
G'(a)=\frac{2}{L(a)}\,G(a)-\mathcal R(a).
\]
Hence, if $a_*\in U$ satisfies
\[
G(a_*)=0,
\]
then
\[
G'(a_*)=-\mathcal R(a_*).
\]

If in addition
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq \mathcal Z(a_*),
\]
then
\[
D_{a_*}''(\tau(a_*))\neq 0,
\qquad
\tau'(a_*)=0,
\qquad
\tau''(a_*)=
-\frac{\mathcal R(a_*)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-\mathcal Z(a_*)}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since
\[
G(a)=V(a)-\mathcal Z(a),
\]
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(1)
gives
\[
G'(a)=V'(a)-\mathcal R(a)
=\frac{2}{\tau(a)-a}\,\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)-\mathcal R(a)
=\frac{2}{L(a)}\,G(a)-\mathcal R(a).
\]
Evaluating at a root $a_*$ of $G$ gives
\[
G'(a_*)=-\mathcal R(a_*).
\]

Now assume also that
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq \mathcal Z(a_*).
\]
Since $G(a_*)=0$, this means
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq V(a_*).
\]
So Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(2)
yields
\[
D_{a_*}''(\tau(a_*))
=
\frac{2}{(\tau(a_*)-a_*)^2}\,
\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-V(a_*)\bigr)
\neq 0.
\]
Then Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(3)
applies near $a_*$ and gives
\[
\tau'(a)
=
\frac{G(a)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)}.
\]
Evaluating at $a_*$ gives
\[
\tau'(a_*)=0.
\]

Differentiate this identity once more. Since $G(a_*)=0$ and
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-V(a_*)=\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-\mathcal Z(a_*)\neq 0,
\]
one gets
\[
\tau''(a_*)
=
\frac{G'(a_*)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-V(a_*)}
=
-\frac{\mathcal R(a_*)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-\mathcal Z(a_*)},
\]
as claimed.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Nondegenerate rooted point is a fold of the moving-shear equation]
\label{prop:nondegenerate-rooted-point-is-moving-shear-fold}
Work in a local normalized nonmixed chart on which
\[
S(t)=t^2.
\]
Define
\[
\mathscr F(a,t):=A_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\,B_a(t)
=(t-a)^2\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
\]
Let
\[
a_*<t_*
\]
satisfy
\[
\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0,
\qquad
\partial_t\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0,
\]
and assume
\[
\mathcal R(a_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\mathcal Z(t_*)\neq \mathcal Z(a_*).
\]
Then
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)
=
-(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*),
\]
and
\[
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)
=
2\bigl(\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)\bigr).
\]
In particular,
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)\neq 0.
\]
Hence near $(a_*,t_*)$ the zero set
\[
\mathscr F(a,t)=0
\]
is the graph of a unique real-analytic function
\[
a=\alpha(t)
\]
with
\[
\alpha(t_*)=a_*,
\qquad
\alpha'(t_*)=0,
\qquad
\alpha''(t_*)
=
\frac{2\bigl(\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)\bigr)}
{(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*)}.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
a-a_*
=
\frac{\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)}
{(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*)}(t-t_*)^2
+o\!\left((t-t_*)^2\right).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since
\[
\mathscr F(a,t)=(t-a)^2\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr),
\]
the conditions
\[
\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0,
\qquad
\partial_t\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0
\]
imply
\[
D_{a_*}(t_*)=\mathcal Z(a_*),
\qquad
D_{a_*}'(t_*)=0.
\]
So $(a_*,t_*)$ is a rooted critical point.

Differentiate $\mathscr F$ with respect to $a$:
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a,t)
=
-2(t-a)\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
+(t-a)^2\bigl(\partial_aD_a(t)-\mathcal R(a)\bigr).
\]
At the rooted point,
\[
D_{a_*}(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)=0,
\]
and by
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch},
\[
\partial_aD_a(t)=\frac{2}{t-a}\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr),
\]
so
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)
=
-(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*).
\]

Next,
\[
\partial_t\mathscr F(a,t)
=
2(t-a)\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
+(t-a)^2D_a'(t),
\]
hence
\[
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a,t)
=
2\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
+4(t-a)D_a'(t)
+(t-a)^2D_a''(t).
\]
At the rooted critical point this becomes
\[
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)
=
(t_*-a_*)^2D_{a_*}''(t_*).
\]
Applying
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(2)
and using
\[
D_{a_*}(t_*)=\mathcal Z(a_*),
\]
one gets
\[
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)
=
2\bigl(\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)\bigr).
\]

By the two nonvanishing assumptions,
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)\neq 0.
\]
So the implicit function theorem gives a unique real-analytic graph
\[
a=\alpha(t)
\]
for the zero set of $\mathscr F$ near $(a_*,t_*)$. Since
\[
\partial_t\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0,
\]
one has
\[
\alpha'(t_*)=0.
\]
Differentiating
\[
\mathscr F(\alpha(t),t)=0
\]
twice at $t=t_*$ gives
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)\,\alpha''(t_*)
+
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0,
\]
hence
\[
\alpha''(t_*)
=
-\frac{\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)}
{\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)}
=
\frac{2\bigl(\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)\bigr)}
{(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*)}.
\]
The Taylor expansion of $\alpha$ then yields the stated quadratic form.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[First rooted point as a post-birth fold problem]
\label{rem:first-rooted-point-post-birth-fold-problem}
Let $b$ be an isolated odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$, and let
\[
t=\tau(a)
\]
be an analytic continuation of the born repeated-source critical branch. By
Proposition~\ref{prop:first-rooting-requires-second-odd-zero-repeated-source},
any first rooted point along this continuation can occur only after the segment
has acquired a second odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$.

At such a rooted point, if
\[
\mathcal R(a_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq \mathcal Z(a_*),
\]
then
Proposition~\ref{prop:rooted-defect-transport-stationary-first-root} shows that
the rooted defect
\[
G(a)=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a)
\qquad
\text{equivalently}\qquad
G(a)=\Psi_a(\sigma(a))-\mathcal Z(a)
\]
crosses transversely and that the target map is stationary there:
\[
\tau'(a_*)=0.
\]
Moreover,
Proposition~\ref{prop:nondegenerate-rooted-point-is-moving-shear-fold} shows
that the moving-shear equation
\[
A_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)\,B_a(x)=0
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
D_{f_a}(a,h)=0,
\quad
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\]
has a local fold at the first rooted point.

Thus the unresolved adjacent-odd-zero issue is not another local odd-zero birth
problem. It is a \emph{post-birth first-fold exclusion problem} for the
source-pinned moving shear $f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda$. The current fixed-level
nonrecurrence results control frozen-$\gamma$ branches on their maximal
slope-overlap blocks, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}
controls the diagonal birth chamber near the seeding odd zero, but neither yet
excludes this first post-birth fold.
\end{remark}
```

## Assistant (2026-04-20 20:08:07)

I’ve narrowed the live target to a much more concrete subproblem: the first rooted point is a stationary point of the continued target map and a fold of the moving-shear equation. The question now is which extra invariant can rule out that first fold.

_Thought for 3m 10s_

Yes. I think there is one genuinely stronger step available, and it may actually kill the current “two-odd-zero” bottleneck.

The key observation is that the moving-shear theorem at a rooted point does not merely say “something special happens.” It says that for
\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\]
a rooted critical point forces at least two interior zeros of
\[
J_{f_a}=(\mathcal Z-\mathcal Z(a))J_\lambda,
\]
so, on a nonmixed arc where \(J_\lambda\neq 0\), it forces at least two interior points
\[
r_1<r_2 \in (a,\tau(a))
\quad\text{with}\quad
\mathcal Z(r_1)=\mathcal Z(a)=\mathcal Z(r_2).
\]

That is much stronger than “the segment has picked up a second odd zero.”

Now combine that with the sign structure of \(\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'\). If \((a,\tau(a))\) contains at most one odd zero of \(\mathcal R\), then the sign of \(\mathcal R\) changes at most once there. Even zeros do not matter for this: they do not change sign. So \(\mathcal Z\) is still unimodal on \([a,\tau(a)]\). A unimodal function can meet a fixed horizontal level in at most two points total. Since one of those points is already the anchor \(a\), there can be at most one interior point \(r>a\) with
\[
\mathcal Z(r)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
So two interior points are impossible.

That gives the theorem I would attack next:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Rooted point forces two interior odd zeros.}
}
\]

More explicitly:

> If \(a<\tau(a)\) satisfies
> \[
> D_a'(\tau(a))=0,
> \qquad
> D_a(\tau(a))=\mathcal Z(a),
> \]
> then \((a,\tau(a))\) must contain at least two odd zeros of \(\mathcal R\).
> Equivalently, at source level, any pair
> \[
> \Psi_a'(\sigma(a))=0,
> \qquad
> \Psi_a(\sigma(a))=\mathcal Z(a)
> \]
> forces at least two odd zeros of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) in the open source interval.

That is stronger than what the draft currently records. Right now the reduction says: first root needs a second odd zero. This would upgrade it to: first root needs **two interior odd zeros**, so a branch born at one odd zero cannot root when it first picks up the next odd zero. It must survive until a **third** odd zero enters the segment.

So the old bottleneck

\[
\text{“adjacent odd-zero connection”}
\]

would be replaced by the sharper bottleneck

\[
\boxed{
\text{“first root requires a third odd zero”}.
}
\]

That is a meaningful advance.

The proof is short if the sheared theorem is already in the strong form the draft seems to suggest.

First, rootedness gives the moving-shear repeated-node tangent-contact event for the frozen level
\[
\gamma=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
By the sheared transfer theorem, this yields at least two interior zeros of
\[
J_{f_a}=(\mathcal Z-\mathcal Z(a))J_\lambda.
\]
Since \(J_\lambda\) does not vanish on the nonmixed arc, these are exactly two interior points where
\[
\mathcal Z(r)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]

Second, suppose \((a,\tau(a))\) had at most one odd zero of \(\mathcal R\). Then \(\mathcal R\) changes sign at most once there, so \(\mathcal Z\) is unimodal on \([a,\tau(a)]\). But a unimodal function cannot hit the level \(\mathcal Z(a)\) at the anchor and at two additional interior points. Contradiction.

That is the whole argument.

The only caveat is this: you need to check that the existing sheared theorem really gives **two distinct interior points** where \(J_{f_a}=0\), not merely two zeros counted with multiplicity or one interior point plus a tangential endpoint phenomenon. If the draft already proves the former, then I think this attack is real and should go in. If the theorem is only stated more loosely, the next step is to tighten that statement, because once it is tightened, the unimodality contradiction is immediate.

If that goes through, then the live remaining source-coupling problem becomes narrower again. It is no longer “can a branch connect adjacent odd zeros?” It becomes:

> can a branch born at one odd zero survive until the segment contains **three** odd zeros and then realize its first post-birth fold?

That is a much smaller and more global configuration.

So I would attack it exactly this way:
prove a clean lemma that “at most one odd zero on the segment implies at most one interior return of \(\mathcal Z\) to the anchor level,” then combine it with the moving-shear repeated-node theorem to get “rooted point forces two interior odd zeros.” If you want, I’ll write the precise LaTeX insertion for that theorem and the downstream summary replacements.
## User (2026-04-20 20:12:04)

attack it

## Assistant (2026-04-20 20:12:08)

I’m checking the exact sheared-transfer statement in the current draft now, because the whole upgrade hinges on whether it already gives two distinct interior anchor-level returns, not just a weaker multiplicity statement.

_Thought for 6m 17s_

I attacked that upgrade, and the honest result is:

**it does not close.**  
The “rooted point forces two interior anchor-level returns” statement is true, but it does **not** upgrade the bottleneck beyond the current two-odd-zero case.

Here is the clean way to see it.

Fix an anchor \(a\) and set
\[
\phi_a(u):=\mathcal Z(u)-\mathcal Z(a),
\qquad
d\mu(u):=\varepsilon S''(u)\,du,
\]
with \(\varepsilon S''>0\) on the nonmixed arc.

For the frozen moving-shear level \(\gamma=\mathcal Z(a)\), define
\[
F_a(x):=\int_a^x \phi_a(u)\,d\mu(u),
\qquad
E_a(x):=\int_a^x (x-u)\phi_a(u)\,d\mu(u).
\]

Then a rooted sheared repeated-node event at \((a,x)\) is exactly
\[
F_a(x)=0,
\qquad
E_a(x)=0,
\]
and of course
\[
E_a'(x)=F_a(x).
\]

So the whole fixed-anchor moving-shear problem is a two-moment cancellation problem.

Now the proposition already in the draft gives the valid consequence:

- if \(F_a(x)=E_a(x)=0\), then either \(\mathcal R\equiv 0\) on \([a,x]\), or there are
  \[
  a<r_1<r_2<x
  \quad\text{with}\quad
  \mathcal Z(r_1)=\mathcal Z(r_2)=\mathcal Z(a).
  \]

That is real. But it is **not enough** to force a third odd zero.

Why not? Because exactly two odd zeros of \(\mathcal R\) already allow this geometry.

If \(\mathcal R\) has exactly two odd zeros on \((a,x)\), then \(\mathcal R\) has sign pattern
\[
\sigma,\ -\sigma,\ \sigma
\]
across three lobes, so \(\mathcal Z\) is monotone on three consecutive intervals. For levels between the middle extremal values, \(\mathcal Z(u)=\mathcal Z(a)\) can indeed have two interior forward solutions \(r_1,r_2\). So the sheared theorem’s conclusion is perfectly compatible with the adjacent-two-odd-zero picture.

And this is not just a geometric possibility. The two moment equations themselves are algebraically compatible with a three-lobe sign pattern.

A concrete model is:
\[
\phi(u)=
\begin{cases}
1,&0<u<1,\\
-2,&1<u<2,\\
1,&2<u<3,
\end{cases}
\qquad
d\mu=du.
\]
Then
\[
\int_0^3 \phi(u)\,du=0,
\qquad
\int_0^3 (3-u)\phi(u)\,du=0.
\]
So
\[
F(3)=0,\qquad E(3)=0,
\]
with exactly two sign changes of \(\phi\). After smoothing, this gives an analytic model with the same feature.

That is the key obstruction: **the frozen-\(a\) shear-transfer identities do not by themselves rule out the exactly-two-odd-zero configuration.**

So the attempted theorem

\[
\text{“first root requires a third odd zero”}
\]

does **not** follow from the current identities. The best valid conclusion remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a rooted point forces the segment to have enough oscillation to produce two interior
returns of the anchor level;}
}
\]
but that oscillation is still compatible with exactly two odd zeros of \(\mathcal R\).

So where does that leave the attack?

It leaves it exactly here:

- the **static** frozen-anchor moment package is exhausted;
- the remaining hope has to use the **dynamic continuation** of the born branch in \(a\), not just one frozen rooted point.

That is why the new transport/fold results matter. They add information the static moment equations do not see:

\[
G(a)=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a),\qquad
G'(a)=\frac{2}{\tau(a)-a}G(a)-\mathcal R(a),
\]
so at a first root,
\[
G(a_*)=0,\qquad G'(a_*)=-\mathcal R(a_*),
\]
and
\[
\tau'(a_*)=0,
\]
with the moving-shear equation having a local fold there.

That is genuinely extra structure. Any further attack has to exploit **that**.

So my honest verdict is:

- I do **not** think the “third odd zero” upgrade is correct.
- I do think the right remaining target is now very specific:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{exactly-two-odd-zero first-fold exclusion.}
}
\]

In words: assume the segment contains exactly two odd zeros, and the continued born branch reaches its first rooted point there. Use the dynamic facts
\[
G'(a_*)=-\mathcal R(a_*),\qquad \tau'(a_*)=0,
\]
plus the fold structure of the moving-shear equation, to show that this first fold cannot occur.

That is narrower than before, but it is a new theorem, not something the current static shear-transfer package already gives for free.

So the attack succeeded in one important way: it showed that the purely static positive-kernel/shear-moment lane is now spent. The only live continuation of this branch is the **dynamic first-fold** problem in the exactly-two-odd-zero configuration.
## User (2026-04-20 20:21:17)

attack exactly-two-odd-zero first-fold exclusion.​

## Assistant (2026-04-20 20:21:19)

I’m going straight at the two-odd-zero fold configuration itself now. Either there’s a real contradiction hidden in the branch transport plus first-fold geometry, or we’ll be able to say cleanly which additional invariant is still missing.

_Thought for 11m 2s_

I attacked it, and the honest result is a **no-go refinement**, not an exclusion theorem.

The key point is: with the current normalized scalar machinery, the exactly-two-odd-zero first-fold configuration is still **formally realizable**. What the attack does give is a sharper statement of what must still be excluded.

Take the normalized nonmixed chart
\[
S(x)=x^2
\]
and define
\[
\mathcal Z(x):=x\Bigl(x-\frac{18-3\sqrt6}{10}\Bigr)\Bigl(x-\frac{18+3\sqrt6}{10}\Bigr)
=
x^3-\frac{18}{5}x^2+\frac{27}{10}x.
\]
Then
\[
\mathcal R(x)=\mathcal Z'(x)=3x^2-\frac{36}{5}x+\frac{27}{10},
\]
so \(\mathcal R\) has exactly two simple zeros,
\[
\xi_1=\frac65-\frac{3\sqrt6}{10},
\qquad
\xi_2=\frac65+\frac{3\sqrt6}{10},
\]
both lying in \((0,3)\).

Now fix the anchor \(a=0\). One checks directly that
\[
\int_0^3 \mathcal Z(u)\,du=0,
\qquad
\int_0^3 (3-u)\mathcal Z(u)\,du=0.
\]
So with the frozen level \(\gamma=\mathcal Z(0)=0\), the pair \((0,3)\) is a rooted sheared repeated-node point:
\[
D_0'(3)=0,
\qquad
D_0(3)=\mathcal Z(0)=0.
\]

In fact here
\[
D_0(x)=\frac{x(x-3)^2}{10},
\]
hence
\[
D_0'(x)=\frac{3x^2-12x+9}{10},
\]
so the two critical points are
\[
x=1,\qquad x=3.
\]
The outer one \(x=3\) is rooted, while the inner one \(x=1\) is not:
\[
D_0(1)=\frac25\neq 0.
\]

Moreover this rooted point is nondegenerate in exactly the sense of the current transport/fold package:
\[
\mathcal R(0)=\frac{27}{10}\neq 0,
\qquad
\mathcal Z(3)-\mathcal Z(0)=\frac{27}{10}\neq 0.
\]
So the first-root formulas would give
\[
G'(0)=-\mathcal R(0)=-\frac{27}{10},
\qquad
\tau'(0)=0,
\qquad
\tau''(0)=-1
\]
along the outer critical branch.

This matters because it shows the following.

There is an explicit analytic normalized model in which:

- the segment contains **exactly two odd zeros** of \(\mathcal R\);
- there is a **nondegenerate rooted fold**;
- and there is also a distinct inner critical point that stays unrooted.

So the present scalar package does **not** force a contradiction in the exactly-two-odd-zero case.

What it does show, very sharply, is that the remaining issue is now a **branch-selection problem**.

In this model, the two critical branches are
\[
\tau_\pm(a)=2-\frac{2a}{3}\pm \frac13\sqrt{(3-a)(5a+3)}.
\]
The lower branch \(\tau_-\) is the one that comes out of the first odd zero:
\[
\tau_-(\xi_1)=\xi_1.
\]
It is the “born” inner branch. The upper branch \(\tau_+\) is the outer one, and at \(a=0\) it gives the rooted fold:
\[
\tau_+(0)=3.
\]

So the actual unresolved theorem is no longer “exclude exactly two odd zeros” in the abstract. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{born-branch separation theorem:}
\text{ the analytic continuation of the branch born at the first odd zero cannot transfer}
\\
\text{to the outer critical branch before rooting.}
}
\]

That is the real content of the attack.

So my verdict is:

- **No**, the current transport + fold + sheared-moment identities do not exclude the exactly-two-odd-zero first fold.
- **Yes**, they reduce the remaining problem to something more specific:

> prove that the **born inner critical branch** cannot jump onto the **outer rooted branch** in the two-odd-zero regime.

That is a much narrower target than before.

The clean next attack would be to look for an invariant that distinguishes the inner and outer critical branches and is preserved under continuation from the seeding odd zero. Candidates would be:
\[
\operatorname{sgn}(\tau(a)-r_2(a)),
\quad
\text{or a source-determinant sign/orientation index,}
\]
or some monotone quantity attached specifically to the born branch.

So the branch is not dead, but the broad scalar route is basically exhausted. The remaining work is a **branch-label / continuation invariant**, not another kernel-moment identity.
## User (2026-04-20 20:34:12)
