## Assistant (2026-04-21 02:30:09)

_Thought for 5m 24s_

Yes. I think there is a genuinely important new result:

\[
\boxed{\textbf{local source-coupling no-go theorem}}
\]

A **nondegenerate rooted point is locally completely generic**. So no theorem that only uses the local germ of the two source equations
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0,
\qquad
D_{f_a}(a,h)=0,
\qquad f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\]
can exclude it.

That is stronger than the earlier four-lobe scalar no-go, because it says the failure is not just in the normalized moment model. It persists even after bringing the actual source equations back in.

---

## 1. The two natural local equations

In the normalized nonmixed chart, set
\[
F(a,t):=D_a'(t),
\qquad
G(a,t):=D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a),
\qquad
H(a,t):=\mathcal Z(t)-D_a(t),
\qquad
L:=t-a.
\]

Then:

- the critical locus is
  \[
  F(a,t)=0,
  \]
- the RH-selected moving-shear slice is
  \[
  G(a,t)=0.
  \]

A rooted point is exactly a common zero
\[
F(a_*,t_*)=0,\qquad G(a_*,t_*)=0.
\]

We already have the exact identities
\[
F_a=\frac{2}{L}F-\frac{2}{L^2}G,
\qquad
F_t=\frac{2}{L^2}H,
\]
and
\[
G_a=\frac{2}{L}G-\mathcal R(a),
\qquad
G_t=F.
\]

So at a rooted point,
\[
F=G=0,
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
F_a(a_*,t_*)=0,\qquad
F_t(a_*,t_*)=\frac{2}{L_*^2}H(a_*,t_*),
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
G_a(a_*,t_*)=-\mathcal R(a_*),\qquad
G_t(a_*,t_*)=0.
}
\]

If the rooted point is nondegenerate, meaning
\[
\mathcal R(a_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
H(a_*,t_*)\neq 0,
\]
then the Jacobian is
\[
\det \frac{\partial(G,F)}{\partial(a,t)}(a_*,t_*)
=
G_aF_t-G_tF_a
=
-\mathcal R(a_*)\cdot \frac{2}{L_*^2}H(a_*,t_*).
\]

So
\[
\boxed{
\det \frac{\partial(G,F)}{\partial(a,t)}(a_*,t_*)\neq 0.
}
\]

---

## 2. Consequence: the pair \((G,F)\) is a local coordinate system

By the analytic inverse function theorem, near any nondegenerate rooted point,
\[
(a,t)\longmapsto (u,v):=(G(a,t),F(a,t))
\]
is a local analytic diffeomorphism.

So in suitable local analytic coordinates,
\[
u=G,\qquad v=F,
\]
the two equations become simply
\[
u=0,\qquad v=0.
\]

That means:

- the critical locus is just the coordinate axis \(v=0\),
- the RH-selected moving-shear slice is just the coordinate axis \(u=0\),
- and the rooted point is their ordinary transverse crossing.

So the local germ is completely generic.

This is the real statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{there is no purely local obstruction left in the planar normalized pair }(G,F).
}
\]

---

## 3. Source-level version

Now pass back to source coordinates.

On the nonmixed patch, the two source equations are the same objects up to nonvanishing analytic factors and reparametrization:

- the critical equation
  \[
  \mathfrak D(a,h)=0
  \]
  is the source-level lift of
  \[
  F(a,t)=0,
  \]
- the moving-shear rooted equation
  \[
  D_{f_a}(a,h)=0
  \]
  is the source-level lift of
  \[
  G(a,t)=0.
  \]

More precisely, after passing through the local source-to-\(x\) parametrization,
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=\kappa(a,h)\,F(a,t(h)),
\qquad
D_{f_a}(a,h)=\eta(a,h)\,G(a,t(h)),
\]
with \(\kappa,\eta\) nonvanishing analytic.

Therefore the source-level Jacobian
\[
\det \frac{\partial(D_{f_a},\mathfrak D)}{\partial(a,h)}
\]
is also nonzero at any nondegenerate rooted point.

So we get the stronger source-level form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{near a nondegenerate rooted point, }
(a,h)\mapsto \bigl(D_{f_a}(a,h),\mathfrak D(a,h)\bigr)
\text{ is a local analytic diffeomorphism.}
}
\]

In other words, the actual source equations themselves have no local incompatibility.

---

## 4. Why this matters

This is a much sharper no-go than the earlier four-lobe model.

The earlier result said:

- the local scalar moment conditions are formally realizable.

This new result says:

- even after reinstating the actual source equations, a nondegenerate rooted point is locally just a generic crossing of two smooth analytic hypersurfaces.

So any attack that tries to kill the branch by looking only at the local germ of
\[
\mathfrak D=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
D_{f_a}=0
\]
near the first dangerous-chamber root is doomed.

That is a real structural finding.

---

## 5. What remains

This means the next theorem cannot be local.

It has to be a **global branch-selection / no-crossing theorem**: something that prevents the *actual continued RH branch* from ever reaching one of these locally generic crossings.

So the remaining problem is now very cleanly this:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{global source-coupled no-crossing theorem for the realized branch.}
}
\]

Not:

- local parity,
- local moment balance,
- local fold shape,
- local source Jacobians.

All of those are now exhausted.

The only live next attack I see is to find a quantity defined **along the continued critical branch**
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h(a))=0
\]
that distinguishes the realized RH branch from an arbitrary local critical branch and cannot vanish when
\[
D_{f_a}(a,h(a))=0.
\]

That quantity would have to be genuinely global, or at least branch-selective, not just a local function of the jet at one point.

So the honest conclusion of this attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local source-coupling is spent; only global source-coupling can still close the branch.}
}
\]

The next thing I would try is to build a **continuation invariant** along the realized critical branch—some sign, winding, or determinant-ratio quantity that is fixed at birth and incompatible with reaching a rooted crossing later.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 02:36:38)

_Thought for 5m 14s_

I pushed on the “global continuation invariant” idea, and I think there is one real structural theorem here.

It does not yet close the branch, but it reduces the remaining problem to a **boundary-phase theorem**.

Let
\[
\mathscr G(a):=e^{-\mathcal A(a)}\bigl(D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr),
\qquad
\mathcal A'(a)=\frac{2}{\tau(a)-a},
\]
along the continued critical branch \(t=\tau(a)\), and let
\[
q_1>q_2>\cdots
\]
be the successive odd anchor zeros of \(\mathcal R\), with post-anchor chambers
\[
I_j=(q_{j+1},q_j),
\qquad
\epsilon_j:=\operatorname{sgn}(\mathcal R|_{I_j})\in\{\pm1\}.
\]

Define the chamber phase
\[
\phi_j:=\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_j)\,\epsilon_j\in\{\pm1\}.
\]
So \(\phi_j=+1\) means the chamber is safe, \(\phi_j=-1\) means dangerous.

Now let
\[
n_j\in\{0,1\}
\]
be the number of rooted crossings on \(I_j\). Because \(\mathscr G\) is monotone on each fixed-sign chamber, \(n_j\) is indeed either \(0\) or \(1\).

Then there are two simple facts:

First,
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_{j+1})=(-1)^{n_j}\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_j),
\]
because no root means the sign is unchanged across the chamber, while one root means it flips exactly once.

Second, since \(q_{j+1}\) is an odd zero,
\[
\epsilon_{j+1}=-\epsilon_j.
\]

Combining them gives the exact phase recursion
\[
\boxed{
\phi_{j+1}=(-1)^{n_j+1}\phi_j.
}
\]

This is the global discrete invariant I was looking for.

Since the first post-anchor chamber is dangerous, you already know
\[
\phi_1=-1.
\]
Therefore, if
\[
N_{m-1}:=\sum_{j=1}^{m-1} n_j
\]
is the total number of rooted crossings before \(q_m\), then
\[
\boxed{
\phi_m=(-1)^{m+N_{m-1}}.
}
\]

So the phase at any later odd anchor zero determines the parity of the total number of rooted crossings up to that point.

That is a real theorem. It means:

- without any rooted crossings, the phases alternate
  \[
  -,+,-,+,\dots
  \]
  as we already knew;
- every rooted crossing **toggles the alternation rule** thereafter.

So the remaining nonmixed problem is now very concrete:

> if you can compute the phase \(\phi_m\) at any distinguished later boundary point of the continued branch, then you know the parity of all rooted crossings that happened before it.

This gives the next attack:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{prove a boundary-phase theorem at branch termination.}
}
\]

There are only a few possible global terminations of the realized branch:

- affine-planar collapse,
- branch exit from the opened nonmixed arc,
- or arrival at some other distinguished source-level boundary.

If one can determine the sign of \(\mathscr G\) there, then the parity formula above gives the total number of rooted crossings. Since each chamber carries at most one crossing and the early chambers are already excluded, that could force zero crossings altogether.

So my next attack would be:

1. identify the actual global endpoint/boundary of the continued born branch in the draft’s setup;
2. compute or constrain the sign of
   \[
   \mathscr G=e^{-\mathcal A}(D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a))
   \]
   there;
3. feed that into
   \[
   \phi_m=(-1)^{m+N_{m-1}}.
   \]

If the endpoint phase agrees with the root-free phase, the whole branch closes.

So the math has moved from “find another local obstruction” to a very specific global target:

\[
\boxed{
\text{boundary sign of the integrating-factor defect } \mathscr G.
}
\]

That is the next attack I’d pursue.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 02:37:17)

I’m testing the “boundary-phase” idea against the actual branch ODE, because it only helps if the endpoint sign of \(\mathscr G\) is determined by the branch’s possible terminal behaviors.

_Thought for 1m 50s_

I attacked the boundary-phase idea, and the honest result is a **global no-go for the transport recursion by itself**.

The exact weighted-defect system is too free to determine the endpoint phase.

Let
\[
x_j:=|\mathscr G(q_j)|>0,
\qquad
\phi_j:=\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_j)\,\epsilon_j\in\{\pm1\},
\qquad
M_j:=\int_{q_{j+1}}^{q_j} e^{-\mathcal A(s)}|\mathcal R(s)|\,ds>0.
\]
Then on chamber \(I_j=(q_{j+1},q_j)\), the exact recursion is:

- if \(\phi_j=+1\) (safe), no root can occur and
  \[
  x_{j+1}=x_j+M_j,
  \qquad
  \phi_{j+1}=-1;
  \]

- if \(\phi_j=-1\) (dangerous) and no root occurs, then
  \[
  0<M_j<x_j,
  \qquad
  x_{j+1}=x_j-M_j,
  \qquad
  \phi_{j+1}=+1;
  \]

- if \(\phi_j=-1\) and a root occurs, then
  \[
  M_j>x_j,
  \qquad
  x_{j+1}=M_j-x_j,
  \qquad
  \phi_{j+1}=-1.
  \]

So once you know \((x_j,\phi_j)\), the next state is completely controlled by the single positive number \(M_j\).

And that means:

\[
\boxed{
\text{any admissible crossing pattern can be realized by a suitable choice of positive masses }M_j.
}
\]

More precisely, start with the forced initial state
\[
\phi_1=-1,\qquad x_1>0.
\]
Take any finite binary sequence \(n_1,\dots,n_{m-1}\) such that \(n_j=0\) whenever \(\phi_j=+1\) and \(n_j\in\{0,1\}\) when \(\phi_j=-1\). Then you can realize it inductively:

- if \(\phi_j=+1\), pick any \(M_j>0\);
- if \(\phi_j=-1\) and you want \(n_j=0\), pick any \(0<M_j<x_j\);
- if \(\phi_j=-1\) and you want \(n_j=1\), pick any \(M_j>x_j\).

This produces exactly the desired root/no-root pattern, and hence any compatible endpoint phase.

So the conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the transport/phase recursion alone cannot determine the boundary phase.}
}
\]

That kills the boundary-phase theorem as a purely recursive attack.

It also clarifies the mathematics:

the remaining obstruction is not a combinatorial parity problem anymore. It is a **mass-selection problem**.

Something genuinely source-coupled has to constrain the actual chamber masses
\[
M_j=\int_{q_{j+1}}^{q_j} e^{-\mathcal A(s)}|\mathcal R(s)|\,ds
\]
so that the “bad” choices \(M_j>x_j\) on dangerous chambers cannot occur.

So the next live theorem target is now very concrete:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{source-coupled mass-selection theorem:}
\text{ on the realized RH branch, the dangerous-chamber masses }M_j
\text{ cannot exceed the incoming defect }x_j.
}
\]

Or a weaker pairwise version:
\[
M_{j+1}\ge M_j
\]
on safe-dangerous pairs, or any inequality that forces the alternating recursion to stay subcritical.

So this attack did produce a useful endpoint:

- local scalar moments are too free;
- local source germs are too generic;
- global phase recursion is also too free.

The only thing left that can close the branch is a genuinely source-coupled restriction on the **actual weighted masses** along the realized critical branch.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 02:40:01)

I’m checking the exact sign statement of the existing odd-zero / unrooted-defect proposition in the draft now, because if its local sign disagrees with the incoming sign from the anchor-sign theorem, that would be the first real route-2 closure.

_Thought for 7m 54s_

I think I found the real closure for route 2.

The key is a **sign clash at the next odd anchor zero**.

Let
\[
G(a):=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a)
\]
along the continued repeated-source critical branch \(t=\tau(a)\).

There are now two facts in the draft that, when combined, look fatal:

1. On the standard adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber, the anchor-sign theorem gives
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a).
\]

2. Near any isolated odd zero \(q\) of \(\mathcal R\), the local odd-zero defect theorem
(`Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}`) gives, along the unique local critical branch,
\[
\Psi_a(\sigma(a))-\mathcal Z(x(a))
=
-\frac{\rho(0)}{2^{m+1}(m+2)}
\bigl(x(\sigma(a))-x(a)\bigr)^{m+1}
+o(\cdots),
\]
so since \(m+1\) is even,
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=-\operatorname{sgn}\rho(0)
\]
for all sufficiently small \(a\neq q\).

But on the **right-hand side** of \(q\),
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a)=\operatorname{sgn}\rho(0).
\]
Therefore, approaching \(q\) from the right, the local theorem says
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=-\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a).
}
\]

That is the opposite of the anchor-sign theorem.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{a safe chamber cannot land at the next odd anchor zero.}
}
\]

That is the real next theorem.

Here is the clean formulation.

---

### Theorem (safe-to-odd-zero exclusion)

Let \(J\) be a genuine opened nonmixed arc, and let \(q\in J\) be an isolated odd zero of \(\mathcal R\). Suppose there is a real-analytic continuation of the repeated-source critical branch
\[
t=\tau(a),\qquad D_a'(\tau(a))=0,
\]
for \(a\in(q,q+\delta)\), such that on \((q,q+\delta)\)
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a).
\]
Then this continuation cannot approach \(q\) within the nonmixed patch.

#### Proof
On the interval \((q,q+\delta)\), the anchor approaches \(q\) from the right.  
Since \(q\) is an odd zero, write locally
\[
\mathcal R(x)=x^m\rho(x),\qquad m\ge1\text{ odd},\quad \rho(0)\neq0.
\]
Then for \(x>0\),
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(x)=\operatorname{sgn}\rho(0).
\]
But `Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}` gives on the unique local critical branch near \(q\)
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=-\operatorname{sgn}\rho(0)
\]
for all sufficiently small \(a\neq q\). Hence for \(a>q\) sufficiently close to \(q\),
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=-\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a),
\]
contradicting the assumed safe-chamber sign relation
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a).
\]
So such a continuation cannot reach \(q\). ∎

---

### Consequence for route 2

The adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber is exactly such a safe chamber: by the current anchor-sign corollary,
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a)
\]
throughout it.

Therefore the continued born branch cannot reach the next odd anchor zero from that chamber.

But every later dangerous post-anchor chamber required the anchor to cross that odd zero first.

So the whole delayed post-anchor scenario never starts.

That means:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{route 2 appears to close.}
}
\]

More explicitly:

- if the opened nonmixed arc has at most one odd zero, you already excluded rooting;
- if it has a next odd zero \(q\), the safe adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber cannot land at \(q\);
- so no post-anchor dangerous chamber can ever be entered;
- hence no rooted crossing can occur anywhere on the continued repeated-source branch inside the genuine opened nonmixed arc.

---

### What I think this means

If the two ingredients above are stated exactly as they now appear in the draft, this is stronger than the earlier “delayed no-crossing / profile-realizability” bottleneck.

It says the branch dies **before** any delayed dangerous chamber becomes relevant.

So the next thing I would do is not keep pushing abstractly. I would audit this sign-clash argument very carefully against the exact hypotheses of:

- `Corollary~\ref{cor:no-crossing-adjacent-two-odd-zero-under-anchor-sign-preservation}`, and
- `Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}`,

especially checking that the local branch near the next odd zero is indeed the same analytic critical branch the continuation would have to land on.

If that check passes, then this is not just “the next attack.” It is probably the route-2 closure.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 02:49:26)

I’m checking the exact hypotheses around the odd-zero local theorem and the anchor-sign corollary now, because the sign-clash only closes route 2 if those two statements really apply to the same continued branch near the next odd zero.

_Thought for 2m 12s_

I think this attack works, with one important directional caveat that actually helps.

The clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{safe chamber cannot land at the next odd anchor zero from the right.}
}
\]

Let \(q\) be an isolated odd zero of \(\mathcal R\), and suppose the continued repeated-source critical branch
\[
h=\sigma(a)\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad t=\tau(a)
\]
approaches \(q\) with the anchor \(a\to q^+\) inside the same good nonmixed patch. Assume on that interval the branch is in a “safe” regime:
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a),
\qquad
G(a):=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a).
\]

Then this is impossible.

Here is the proof.

Center the local \(x\)-coordinate at \(q\), so
\[
x(q)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=x^m\rho(x),
\qquad
m\ge 1 \text{ odd},\quad \rho(0)\neq 0.
\]

Because \(m\) is odd, on the **right-hand side** of \(q\) one has
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(x)=\operatorname{sgn}\rho(0).
\]

Now use
\[
\text{Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}}.
\]
It says that near \(q\) the critical locus is the graph of a **unique** real-analytic branch
\[
h=\sigma(a),
\]
and along that branch
\[
\Psi_a(\sigma(a))-\mathcal Z(x(a))
=
-\frac{\rho(0)}{2^{m+1}(m+2)}
\bigl(x(\sigma(a))-x(a)\bigr)^{m+1}
+o(\cdots).
\]
Since \(m+1\) is even,
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(\Psi_a(\sigma(a))-\mathcal Z(x(a))\bigr)
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\rho(0)
\]
for all sufficiently small \(a\neq q\).

But on the actual branch,
\[
\Psi_a(\sigma(a))-\mathcal Z(x(a))
\]
is exactly the source version of
\[
G(a)=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a),
\]
so near \(q\),
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=-\operatorname{sgn}\rho(0).
\]

Approaching \(q\) from the right, this becomes
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=-\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a),
\]
which contradicts the safe-chamber relation
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a).
\]

So a safe chamber cannot continue into an odd zero from the right.

That directional caveat matters: on the **left** side of an odd zero,
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(x)=-\operatorname{sgn}\rho(0),
\]
so the local odd-zero theorem would give
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a),
\]
and there would be no clash. But along this route the anchor is being continued toward smaller \(a\), so the next odd anchor zero is reached from the **right**, which is exactly the contradictory side.

So the consequence is strong:

- the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber is safe by the anchor-sign corollary;
- therefore it cannot land at the next odd anchor zero from the right;
- hence the whole delayed post-anchor scenario never starts.

That means route 2 appears to close.

I would state the closure like this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{On a genuine opened nonmixed arc, the continued born repeated-source branch cannot realize a rooted crossing.}
}
\]

The logic is now:

1. one-sign-change chambers are sterile;
2. the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber is root-free and safe;
3. a safe chamber cannot reach the next odd anchor zero from the right;
4. therefore no post-anchor dangerous chamber is ever entered;
5. so no rooted crossing can occur anywhere along the continued branch.

The only thing I would still audit carefully before treating this as finished is the identification step:

- near the odd zero \(q\), the global continued critical branch must indeed be the same local branch as the unique \(\sigma(a)\) from `prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect`;
- and the quantity in that proposition must match the same \(G(a)\) used in the anchor-sign corollary via the source/planar reformulation.

If those two identifications are already clean in the draft, then this is not just the next attack. It is probably the actual route-2 closure.

_Thought for 2m 39s_

Yes. I audited those two identification steps separately.

My conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{\text{the quantity identification works, but the branch identification does \emph{not} yet follow from the draft.}}
\]

So the proposed route-2 closure by sign clash is **not yet justified** as written.

---

## 1) The quantity identification is already in the draft

This part is fine.

The draft gives, in `Remark~\ref{rem:source-determinant-reformulation-Gammaa}`,
\[
\Psi_a(h)=\Gamma_{x(a)}(x(h)).
\]
So once you pass from source coordinates to the local \(x\)-coordinate on the nonmixed patch, the source defect
\[
\Psi_a(h)-\mathcal Z(x(a))
\]
is exactly the planar defect
\[
\Gamma_{x(a)}(x(h))-\mathcal Z(x(a)).
\]

Along a critical branch, if you write the planar target as
\[
\tau(x(a)):=x(h),
\]
then this is precisely
\[
D_{x(a)}(\tau(x(a)))-\mathcal Z(x(a)),
\]
i.e. the same \(G\) used in the anchor-sign theorem.

And in `Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}(2)`, the draft gives the exact identity
\[
D_{f_a}(a,h)
=
D_\lambda(a,h)\bigl(\Psi_a(h)-\mathcal Z(x(a))\bigr),
\qquad
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(x(a))\lambda.
\]
So the source-pinned moving-shear numerator is exactly the same defect, up to the nonvanishing factor \(D_\lambda(a,h)\).

So this part of the proposed sign-clash argument is sound:

- `anchor-sign` talks about the sign of
  \[
  G(a)=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a),
  \]
- `prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect` talks about the sign of
  \[
  \Psi_a(\sigma(a))-\mathcal Z(x(a)),
  \]
- and those are the same quantity once the two branches are identified.

That identification is already present in the draft.

---

## 2) The branch identification is **not** yet in the draft

This is the gap.

The local odd-zero proposition
`Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}`
only proves a unique local branch
\[
h=\sigma(a)
\]
for the critical locus **inside a small neighborhood of the diagonal point**
\[
(a,h)=(q,q).
\]

Its item (1) says the critical locus near the odd zero \(q\) is the graph of a unique real-analytic branch with
\[
\sigma(q)=q,
\qquad
\sigma(a)\neq a.
\]

But to use that proposition on the **global continued branch**, you still need to know that when the anchor tends to \(q\), the target also tends to \(q\), so that the global branch actually enters that local neighborhood.

That is exactly what the current draft does **not** prove.

The present route-2 arguments give:

- on a fixed-sign anchor interval, no rooting can occur;
- after an anchor odd zero, there is no immediate reset;
- dangerous/safe post-anchor chambers alternate;
- local scalar and even local source-germ data are too weak to exclude a later crossing.

But none of that shows:

\[
a\to q^+ \quad\Longrightarrow\quad h(a)\to q
\]
along the continued branch.

And without that, the global branch could in principle approach the vertical line \(a=q\) while the target remains far away:
\[
(a,h(a))\to(q,h_*)\qquad\text{with }h_*\neq q.
\]

In that case the local odd-zero theorem near \((q,q)\) says nothing, because the branch is not entering its neighborhood.

So the safe-to-odd-zero sign clash only works if you add a new lemma of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Diagonal landing lemma: }\;
\text{if the continued born critical branch approaches an odd anchor zero }q
\text{ inside the same nonmixed patch, then }h(a)\to q.
}
\]

Or at least a weaker version:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the global branch must enter the local box where }
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\text{ is represented by }h=\sigma(a).
}
\]

That statement is not currently proved.

---

## 3) So the sign-clash closure is not yet valid

Because of that missing branch-capture step, the current argument

- uses the correct defect quantity,
- but applies the local odd-zero sign law to a branch that has not yet been shown to be the same branch.

So at present, the draft does **not** justify:

\[
\text{safe chamber} \;\Longrightarrow\; \text{cannot land at next odd anchor zero from the right}.
\]

What it does justify is narrower:

> if the continued branch **does** enter the local diagonal neighborhood of the next odd zero, then it must coincide with the unique local branch \(h=\sigma(a)\), and then the sign clash is real.

That conditional statement is fine.

---

## 4) The exact extra theorem you need

The missing step is now very clear.

You need one more source-coupled lemma, something like:

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Diagonal capture near an odd anchor zero]
Let $q$ be an isolated odd zero of $\mathcal R$ on a good nonmixed patch, and
let $(a,h(a))$ be a real-analytic continuation of the born repeated-source
critical branch with
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h(a))=0,
\qquad a>q,
\qquad a\to q^+.
\]
Assume the branch remains in the same nonmixed patch and does not exit or
collapse affine-planarly. Then
\[
h(a)\to q.
\]
Hence for $a$ sufficiently close to $q$, the branch coincides with the unique
local branch $h=\sigma(a)$ from
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}.
\end{lemma}
```

Once you have that, the sign-clash closure goes through.

Without it, there is still an escape route:
the branch could approach the anchor odd zero with a nonlocal target.

---

## 5) Bottom line

My audit result is:

- **Yes**, the defect in the local odd-zero proposition is the same \(G\) from the anchor-sign corollary, after the source/planar conversion already in the draft.
- **No**, the draft does not yet prove that the global continued branch near the next odd anchor zero is the same local branch \(h=\sigma(a)\).

So I would **not** claim route 2 is closed yet.

I would update the route-2 bottleneck to:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{diagonal-capture near the next odd anchor zero.}
}
\]

If that lemma can be proved, then the sign clash probably finishes the branch.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 02:57:19)

I’m attacking the diagonal-capture lemma directly now. I need to see whether the draft already contains enough compactness/first-contact machinery to force \(h(a)\to q\), or whether there is still a genuine escape where the target stays nonlocal.

_Thought for 6m 21s_

I attacked it, and the honest result is:

\[
\boxed{\text{the diagonal-capture lemma is false under the current hypotheses.}}
\]

So that route-2 closure by sign clash cannot be completed as stated.

Here is a concrete **source-level counterexample**.

---

## 1. A normalized source model

Take
\[
c(t)=1,\qquad v_5(t)=t,\qquad \lambda(t)=t^2.
\]
Then
\[
x(t)=\frac{v_5}{c}=t,\qquad S(t)=\frac{\lambda}{c}=t^2,\qquad J_\lambda=W(c,v_5,\lambda)=2,
\]
so this is a good nonmixed patch on every interval.

Now set
\[
\mathcal R(t):=t(t-1)(t^2-4t-2)
=t^4-5t^3+2t^2+2t,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal Z(t):=\int_0^t \mathcal R(u)\,du
=
\frac15 t^5-\frac54 t^4+\frac23 t^3+t^2.
\]
Choose \(u_5=\widetilde Y\) so that
\[
\frac12\,u_5''=\mathcal Z.
\]

Then the odd zeros of \(\mathcal R\) are
\[
2-\sqrt6,\qquad 0,\qquad 1,\qquad 2+\sqrt6.
\]
Let
\[
q:=2-\sqrt6\approx -0.4494897428.
\]
This is the odd zero immediately to the left of \(0\).

In this normalized source model,
\[
\Psi_a(h)=\Gamma_a(h)=D_a(h),
\]
and the critical equation
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\]
is exactly
\[
\partial_h \Psi_a(h)=0.
\]

So this is not just a planar toy: it is literally a source-level model with
\[
\Psi_a(h)=\frac{D_{u_5}(a,h)}{D_\lambda(a,h)}.
\]

---

## 2. The critical equation

Define
\[
F(a,h):=\partial_h\Psi_a(h)=D_a'(h).
\]
A direct calculation gives
\[
F(a,h)
=
\frac{1}{210}\Bigl(
10a^4+16a^3h-70a^3+18a^2h^2-105a^2h+42a^2
\]
\[
\qquad\qquad
+16ah^3-105ah^2+56ah+70a
+10h^4-70h^3+42h^2+70h
\Bigr).
\]

Now look on the compact rectangle
\[
q\le a\le 0,\qquad 0\le h\le \frac25.
\]

At the lower edge,
\[
F(a,0)=\frac{a(5a^3-35a^2+21a+35)}{105}.
\]
Since \(a<0\) and the cubic factor is positive on \([q,0]\), one has
\[
F(a,0)<0
\qquad (q\le a<0).
\]

At the upper edge,
\[
F\!\left(a,\frac25\right)
=
\frac{625a^4-3975a^3+180a^2+4789a+1906}{13125}.
\]
That quartic has no real root on \([q,0]\), and is positive there; hence
\[
F\!\left(a,\frac25\right)>0
\qquad (q\le a\le 0).
\]

So by the intermediate value theorem, for every \(a\in[q,0)\) there is at least one
\[
h(a)\in\left(0,\frac25\right)
\]
with
\[
F(a,h(a))=0.
\]

Now differentiate:
\[
F_h(a,h)
=
\frac{1}{210}\Bigl(
16a^3+36a^2h-105a^2+48ah^2-210ah+56a
+40h^3-210h^2+84h+70
\Bigr).
\]
A direct check on the same rectangle shows
\[
F_h(a,h)>0
\qquad
\text{for }q\le a\le 0,\ 0\le h\le \frac25.
\]
So the root in \(\left(0,\frac25\right)\) is unique, and depends real-analytically on \(a\). Call it
\[
h=\tau(a).
\]

Because near \(a=0^-\) the born branch from the odd zero \(0\) satisfies
\[
\tau(a)=-a+O(a^2),
\]
this unique branch on \([q,0)\) is exactly the **continued born branch**.

---

## 3. What happens at the next odd anchor zero

Since \(\tau(a)\in\left(0,\frac25\right)\) for every \(a\in[q,0)\), letting \(a\to q^+\) gives
\[
\tau(q)\in\left(0,\frac25\right).
\]
In particular,
\[
\boxed{\tau(q)\neq q.}
\]

Numerically,
\[
\tau(q)\approx 0.3540339256.
\]

So the continued born branch approaches the next odd anchor zero \(q\) from the right while staying in the same good nonmixed patch, but the target does **not** land diagonally at \(q\). It lands at a nonlocal point \(h_*=\tau(q)>0\).

That is exactly the negation of the diagonal-capture lemma.

---

## 4. Consequence

So the statement

\[
a\to q^+ \text{ along the continued born branch}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
h(a)\to q
\]

is false in general, even in a normalized source model where

- \(J_\lambda\neq 0\),
- everything is analytic,
- the branch is genuinely the continued born branch,
- and the branch remains in the same nonmixed patch.

Therefore the proposed sign-clash closure is not available under the current hypotheses.

The situation is:

- the **quantity identification** is fine:
  \[
  \Psi_a(h)-\mathcal Z(x(a))
  \]
  is the same defect as
  \[
  G(a)=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a)
  \]
  after source/planar conversion;

- but the **branch identification** fails:
  the continued born branch need not enter the local diagonal neighborhood \((q,q)\), so it need not coincide with the unique local branch \(h=\sigma(a)\) from the odd-zero theorem.

So the “safe chamber cannot land at the next odd anchor zero from the right” claim is only true **conditionally**:

> if the continued branch is known to enter the local diagonal box near \((q,q)\), then the sign clash works.

Without that extra capture hypothesis, it is false.

---

## 5. What this means for the next attack

The missing theorem is not “prove diagonal capture,” because that theorem is false.

The next viable target has to be narrower, something like:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{nonlocal-target exclusion near the next odd anchor zero}
}
\]

In other words: if the continued born branch approaches an odd anchor zero \(q\) with a nonlocal target \(h_*\neq q\), prove that this is incompatible with the actual RH source-coupled structure.

That would be a genuinely source-coupled theorem, and it is now the real bottleneck.

If you want, I’ll turn this into exact LaTeX insertions replacing the draft’s current route-2 bottleneck with this sharper no-go/counterexample statement.

I attacked it, and I think the right honest result is a **stronger no-go theorem for the current route-2 package**.

The key point is that once nonlocal-target landing is allowed, the whole current route-2 story is still formally realizable in an explicit analytic source model. So the present source-coupling package is not enough to close the branch.

Here is the model.

Take
\[
c(t)=1,\qquad v_5(t)=t,\qquad \lambda(t)=t^2,
\]
so
\[
x(t)=t,\qquad S(t)=t^2,\qquad J_\lambda=2\neq 0
\]
on all of \(\mathbf R\).

Now choose
\[
\mathcal R(t)=t(t-1)(t^2-4t-2)
=t^4-5t^3+2t^2+2t,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal Z(t)=\int_0^t \mathcal R(u)\,du
=\frac15 t^5-\frac54 t^4+\frac23 t^3+t^2.
\]
Let \(u_5=\widetilde Y\) be chosen so that
\[
\frac12\,u_5''=\mathcal Z.
\]

Then this is a genuine normalized source model, and
\[
\Psi_a(h)=\Gamma_a(h)=D_a(h),
\qquad
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\iff
\partial_h D_a(h)=0.
\]

Now let
\[
q:=2-\sqrt6\approx -0.4494897428,
\]
the odd zero of \(\mathcal R\) immediately to the left of \(0\).

Define
\[
F(a,h):=\partial_h D_a(h).
\]
A direct computation gives
\[
F(a,h)
=
\frac1{210}\Bigl(
10a^4+16a^3h-70a^3+18a^2h^2-105a^2h+42a^2
\]
\[
\qquad\qquad
+16ah^3-105ah^2+56ah+70a
+10h^4-70h^3+42h^2+70h
\Bigr).
\]

Now look on the rectangle
\[
q\le a\le 0,\qquad 0\le h\le \frac25.
\]

One checks:

\[
F(a,0)<0
\qquad (q\le a<0),
\]
\[
F\!\left(a,\frac25\right)>0
\qquad (q\le a\le 0),
\]
and
\[
F_h(a,h)>0
\qquad
\text{for }q\le a\le 0,\ 0\le h\le \frac25.
\]

So for every \(a\in[q,0)\) there is a unique analytic branch
\[
h=\tau(a)\in\left(0,\frac25\right)
\]
with
\[
F(a,\tau(a))=0.
\]

Near \(a=0^-\), this is exactly the born branch from the odd zero \(0\):
\[
\tau(a)=-a-\frac25a^2-\frac4{25}a^3+O(a^4).
\]

So this branch is the actual continued born branch.

Now the crucial facts.

First, as \(a\to q^+\),
\[
\tau(a)\to \tau(q)\approx 0.3540339256\neq q.
\]
So the branch reaches the next odd anchor zero **nonlocally**. This kills diagonal capture.

Second, along this whole interval \(a\in(q,0)\),
\[
G(a):=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a)<0,
\]
while also
\[
\mathcal R(a)<0.
\]
So the anchor-sign safe relation
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a)
\]
holds all the way down to the next odd anchor zero from the right.

Third, after crossing \(q\), the branch continues analytically with the same nonlocal target branch, and the defect keeps its sign immediately after passage:
\[
G(a)<0
\quad\text{for }a<q\text{ close to }q,
\]
while now
\[
\mathcal R(a)>0.
\]
So this realizes the odd-anchor no-reset picture exactly.

Fourth, the branch then undergoes a **delayed rooted crossing** at
\[
a_*\approx -0.5805673462,\qquad
\tau(a_*)\approx 0.3888336023,
\]
where
\[
F(a_*,\tau(a_*))=0,
\qquad
G(a_*)=0.
\]

So this one explicit normalized source model realizes all of the following at once:

- born-branch continuation from an odd zero;
- safe chamber down to the next odd anchor zero;
- nonlocal-target landing at that anchor zero;
- odd-anchor no-reset;
- and a delayed rooted crossing after the anchor zero.

That means the current route-2 package is still too weak.

The big structural lesson is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{once nonlocal-target landing is allowed, the current anchor-sign / odd-anchor / discriminant analysis does not close the branch.}
}
\]

And there is an important correction to the earlier chamber language:

because the target can stay nonlocal, **crossing an odd anchor zero does not force the active segment to enter the “next odd-zero-count chamber” in the naive way**. In this model, after the anchor crosses \(q\), the segment \([a,\tau(a)]\) contains \(q\) and \(0\), so the delayed root already happens with just those two odd zeros active. So the previous “first dangerous chamber has three odd zeros” intuition is not robust once nonlocal landing is admitted.

So my honest verdict is:

- the proposed diagonal-capture closure is false;
- more than that, the whole current route-2 package admits an explicit analytic source-level countermodel;
- therefore the next attack cannot be a refinement of the same package.

The next live theorem has to exclude **this kind of nonlocal-target continuation** using something not present in the current draft.

The most plausible target now is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{nonlocal-target exclusion theorem:}
\]
\[
\text{on the actual RH branch, if }a\to q^+\text{ to an odd anchor zero, then the target cannot stay in a distant compact subinterval of the same nonmixed patch.}
}
\]

Because the countermodel shows exactly that distant target behavior is what keeps route 2 alive.

So the attack did produce something real: it identifies a concrete analytic counterexample to the current route-2 strategy, and it isolates the only remaining way to salvage that route — a genuinely new theorem excluding nonlocal-target landing on the actual RH branch.

_Thought for 1m 53s_

I think the next honest attack is a **universality / no-go theorem** for route 2.

It is stronger than the explicit quartic counterexample. It says the whole current route-2 source package is still too universal to close the branch.

---

## 1. Universal normalized source realization

Let \(I\subset \mathbf R\) be any interval, and let
\[
\mathcal Z:I\to \mathbf R
\]
be any real-analytic function. Set
\[
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'.
\]

Define source functions on \(I\) by
\[
c(t):=1,\qquad v_5(t):=t,\qquad \lambda(t):=t^2,
\]
and choose \(u_5\) so that
\[
u_5''(t)=2\mathcal Z(t).
\]

Then this is a genuine analytic source model, and the basic source objects collapse to the normalized planar ones.

Indeed, since
\[
J_f=W(c,v_5,f)=W(1,t,f)=f'',
\]
one gets
\[
J_\lambda=2,\qquad J_{u_5}=2\mathcal Z,
\]
hence
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
=
2(2\mathcal Z')-2\mathcal Z\cdot 0
=
4\mathcal R.
\]

Also
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}=t,\qquad S=\frac{\lambda}{c}=t^2,\qquad Y=\frac{u_5}{c}=u_5,
\]
so the planar normalized curve is literally
\[
(x,S,Y)=(t,t^2,u_5(t)).
\]

Therefore all the current route-2 source objects reduce exactly to the normalized planar objects:

- \(\Psi_a(h)=\Gamma_a(h)=D_a(h)\),
- the critical equation \(\mathfrak D(a,h)=0\) is exactly
  \[
  \partial_h D_a(h)=0,
  \]
- and for
  \[
  f_a:=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda
  \]
  one has
  \[
  J_{f_a}=2(\mathcal Z-\mathcal Z(a)).
  \]

So every analytic normalized planar model is realized by a genuine analytic source model with the current source-level package.

That is the theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Universal realization theorem.}
\quad
\text{Any analytic normalized planar profile }\mathcal Z
\text{ lifts to a genuine analytic source model}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
(c,v_5,\lambda,u_5)=(1,t,t^2,u_5)
\text{ for which the current route-2 source objects coincide with the planar ones.}
}
\]

---

## 2. Consequence for the current route-2 package

This means any argument that only uses the present route-2 objects

\[
(c,v_5,\lambda,u_5),\qquad
\Psi_a,\qquad
\mathfrak D,\qquad
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},\qquad
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\]
together with the local analytic manipulations already in the draft, cannot exclude any configuration that already occurs in some analytic normalized planar model.

But the quartic model from the previous attack gives exactly such a configuration:

- a born critical branch from an odd zero;
- a safe adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber;
- nonlocal-target landing at the next odd anchor zero;
- odd-anchor no-reset;
- and a delayed rooted crossing after that anchor zero.

Because that planar model lifts to a genuine source model by the theorem above, the current route-2 source package admits it formally.

So we get the real no-go statement:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Route 2 cannot close using only the current source package }
(c,v_5,\lambda,u_5)\text{ and its present derived identities.}
}
\]

This is stronger than saying “the diagonal-capture lemma is false.” It says:

> even after reinstating the current source objects, the entire delayed-crossing scenario is still realizable.

So the remaining theorem cannot be a refinement of the same package.

---

## 3. What this means mathematically

The current route-2 ingredients are all **universal under normalization**.

They know about:

- the normalized profile \(\mathcal Z\),
- its derivative \(\mathcal R\),
- the critical equation,
- the moving-shear equation,
- and the source Wronskian.

But they do **not** know anything specifically RH-originating beyond that.

So any closure theorem must use some ingredient that is **not universal** under the realization
\[
(c,v_5,\lambda,u_5)=(1,t,t^2,u_5).
\]

That is now the clean dividing line.

---

## 4. The next attack

So the next attack should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{find the first genuinely non-universal RH/source-coupled ingredient.}
}
\]

In practice that means something involving data beyond the current route-2 quartet \((c,v_5,\lambda,u_5)\), for example a relation tying this branch to higher source layers or another structural identity that fails in the universal model above.

A good test for any proposed new ingredient is immediate:

> can it still be realized in the universal model \(c=1,\ v_5=t,\ \lambda=t^2,\ u_5''=2\mathcal Z\)?

If yes, it will not close route 2.  
If no, then it is finally using genuinely RH-specific structure.

So my honest assessment now is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the repeated-source / discriminant branch is reduced as far as it can go with the present source package.}
}
\]

The next useful work is not another sign argument inside route 2. It is to identify the first non-universal structural relation and bring that into the branch.

## 2) Replace `Remark~\ref{rem:no-go-local-scalar-first-dangerous-chamber}`

The current version is too tied to a four-lobe picture, which is no longer robust once nonlocal-target landing is admitted.

Replace the entire remark


with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[No-go for purely local scalar exclusion on the first dangerous post-anchor chamber]
\label{rem:no-go-local-scalar-first-dangerous-chamber}
At a rooted critical point, after normalizing the active interval to
\[
x=a+sL,
\qquad
0\le s\le 1,
\qquad
L=\tau(a)-a,
\]
the profile
\[
R_a(s):=\mathcal R(a+sL)
\]
satisfies the two local scalar moment identities
\[
\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_a(s)\,ds=0,
\qquad
\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_a(s)\,ds=0.
\]

Once nonlocal-target landing is admitted, the first dangerous post-anchor
chamber need not correspond to a fixed odd-zero count or to a rigid four-lobe
pattern on the active segment. Even in the simplest three-lobe sign pattern
\[
+,-,+
\]
(or its global negative), the local scalar rooted equations are already
formally realizable.

Indeed, for any $A>0$, define
\[
R_A(s):=
\begin{cases}
A, & 0<s<\frac13,\\[4pt]
-\frac72 A, & \frac13<s<\frac23,\\[4pt]
\frac{11}{2}A, & \frac23<s<1.
\end{cases}
\]
A direct calculation gives
\[
\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_A(s)\,ds=0,
\qquad
\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_A(s)\,ds=0,
\]
and also
\[
\int_0^1 R_A(s)\,ds
=
\int_0^1 s\,R_A(s)\,ds
=
\int_0^1 s^2\,R_A(s)\,ds
=
A.
\]
So the local rooted-point equations and the nondegenerate fold data are already
formally compatible with a three-lobe profile.

Thus no argument using only the local normalized rooted profile, the two
vanishing scalar moments, and the local transversality/fold signs can exclude
rooting on the first dangerous post-anchor chamber. Any successful next step
must use genuinely source-coupled structure invisible in the planar normalized
$D_a$ model.
\end{remark}
```

## 3) Replace `Remark~\ref{rem:route-two-reduces-to-global-no-crossing}`

```latex
\begin{remark}[What route 2 now reduces to]
```

with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[What route 2 now reduces to]
\label{rem:route-two-reduces-to-global-no-crossing}
The discriminant analysis first showed that a rooted point is not born
\emph{at the entry} into the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber. The stronger
anchor-sign argument showed more: on any continuation interval on which the
anchor-side value
\[
\mathcal R(a)
\]
keeps a fixed sign, the RH-selected slice
\[
\gamma=\mathcal Z(a)
\]
cannot cross the discriminant curve at all.

The odd-anchor analysis sharpened this further: when the anchor itself passes
through an odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$, the integrating-factor defect
\[
\mathscr G(a)=e^{-\mathcal A(a)}\bigl(D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
\]
keeps its incoming sign across that odd anchor zero, so a rooted crossing cannot
occur there or immediately after passage. The subsequent post-anchor chambers
then alternate dangerous and safe, beginning with a dangerous first post-anchor
chamber
(Corollary~\ref{cor:first-post-anchor-chamber-dangerous}).

However, two no-go facts are now clear. First,
Remark~\ref{rem:no-go-local-scalar-first-dangerous-chamber} shows that already
on that first dangerous post-anchor chamber, the local normalized rooted
equations and fold data are formally realizable in the planar scalar model.
Second, the current route-2 source package itself is still universal under the
normalized lift
\[
c=1,\qquad v_5=t,\qquad \lambda=t^2,\qquad u_5''=2\mathcal Z
\]
(Proposition~\ref{prop:universality-threshold-current-route-two-package} below),
so even the source-level objects
\[
\Psi_a,\qquad \mathfrak D,\qquad \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},\qquad D_{f_a}
\]
do not yet distinguish the RH branch from an arbitrary analytic normalized
model.

So route 2 no longer reduces merely to a delayed no-crossing /
profile-realizability problem \emph{within the current package}. It reduces to
finding the first genuinely \emph{non-universal} source-coupled input, i.e. an
ingredient not already captured by the normalized planar $D_a$ model.
\end{remark}
```

## 4) Insert the universality-threshold package

Insert this block **immediately after** `Remark~\ref{rem:route-two-reduces-to-global-no-crossing}` and **before** `\begin{remark}[What remains on the nonmixed $4$-point side]`.

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Universality threshold for the current route-2 package]
\label{prop:universality-threshold-current-route-two-package}
Let $I\subset\mathbf R$ be an interval, let
\[
\mathcal Z:I\to\mathbf R
\]
be real-analytic, and set
\[
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'.
\]
Define analytic source functions on $I$ by
\[
c(t):=1,\qquad v_5(t):=t,\qquad \lambda(t):=t^2,
\]
and choose $u_5$ so that
\[
u_5''(t)=2\mathcal Z(t).
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}=t,
\qquad
S=\frac{\lambda}{c}=t^2,
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}=u_5;
\]

\item for every analytic $f$,
\[
J_f=W(c,v_5,f)=W(1,t,f)=f'',
\]
hence
\[
J_\lambda=2,
\qquad
J_{u_5}=2\mathcal Z,
\qquad
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
=
4\mathcal R;
\]

\item the repeated-source ratio is exactly the normalized planar one:
\[
\Psi_a(h)=\Gamma_a(h)=D_a(h);
\]

\item the critical determinant equation is exactly the normalized planar
critical-point equation:
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\iff
\partial_h \Psi_a(h)=0
\iff
\partial_h D_a(h)=0;
\]

\item for the source-pinned moving shear
\[
f_a:=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\]
one has
\[
J_{f_a}=2(\mathcal Z-\mathcal Z(a)),
\]
and
\[
D_{f_a}(a,h)=D_\lambda(a,h)\bigl(\Psi_a(h)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
\]
\end{enumerate}
Thus every analytic normalized planar model \((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R,D_a)\)
lifts to a genuine analytic source model for the entire current route-2 package.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The identities
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}=t,\qquad
S=\frac{\lambda}{c}=t^2,\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}=u_5
\]
are immediate. Also,
\[
J_f=W(c,v_5,f)=W(1,t,f)=f'',
\]
so
\[
J_\lambda=2,\qquad J_{u_5}=2\mathcal Z.
\]
Hence
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
=
2(2\mathcal Z')-2\mathcal Z\cdot 0
=
4\mathcal R.
\]

Because the source coordinate and the normalized planar coordinate coincide,
\[
x(t)=t,
\]
the source repeated-source quotient is exactly the planar normalized quadratic
envelope:
\[
\Psi_a(h)=\Gamma_a(h)=D_a(h).
\]
Therefore the source critical determinant equation is exactly the planar
critical-point equation
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\iff
\partial_h D_a(h)=0.
\]

Finally,
\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda
\]
satisfies
\[
J_{f_a}=u_5''-2\mathcal Z(a)=2(\mathcal Z-\mathcal Z(a)),
\]
and
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}(2)
gives
\[
D_{f_a}(a,h)=D_\lambda(a,h)\bigl(\Psi_a(h)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
\]
So all route-2 source objects reduce exactly to the normalized planar ones.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[The current route-2 package is universal under normalization]
\label{cor:current-route-two-package-universal-under-normalization}
Any configuration formally realizable by an analytic normalized planar model
\[
(\mathcal Z,\mathcal R,D_a)
\]
is also formally realizable by a genuine analytic source model for the current
route-2 package
\[
(c,v_5,\lambda,u_5),\qquad
\Psi_a,\qquad
\mathfrak D,\qquad
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},\qquad
D_{f_a}.
\]
Accordingly, no contradiction theorem phrased only in terms of the current
route-2 package can distinguish the RH branch from an arbitrary analytic
normalized planar model.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
This is immediate from
Proposition~\ref{prop:universality-threshold-current-route-two-package}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Explicit source-level countermodel to the current route-2 package]
\label{rem:explicit-source-level-countermodel-current-route-two}
Take
\[
\mathcal R(t):=t(t-1)(t^2-4t-2)
\]
and
\[
\mathcal Z(t):=\int_0^t \mathcal R(u)\,du
=
\frac15 t^5-\frac54 t^4+\frac23 t^3+t^2,
\]
and realize this normalized planar model by
\[
c(t)=1,\qquad v_5(t)=t,\qquad \lambda(t)=t^2,\qquad u_5''(t)=2\mathcal Z(t).
\]
Let
\[
q:=2-\sqrt6.
\]
In this genuine analytic source model, the unique born repeated-source critical
branch from the odd zero \(0\) continues analytically down to \(a=q\), lands
there with a nonlocal target
\[
\tau(q)\approx 0.3540339256\neq q,
\]
satisfies the anchor-sign safe relation on \((q,0)\), crosses the odd anchor
zero \(q\) with no sign reset, and then undergoes a delayed rooted crossing at
\[
a_*\approx -0.5805673462,
\qquad
\tau(a_*)\approx 0.3888336023.
\]
Thus diagonal capture fails, and the whole delayed-crossing scenario is
realized inside a genuine analytic source model for the current route-2
package.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The next live target must be non-universal]
\label{rem:next-live-target-must-be-non-universal}
By
Corollary~\ref{cor:current-route-two-package-universal-under-normalization},
the present route-2 package is exhausted: any further progress must use a
genuinely non-universal source-coupled input, i.e. an ingredient not already
absorbed by the normalized planar model \((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R,D_a)\).

Within the current draft, the first canonical candidates for such genuinely
non-universal input lie above the present route-2 package, for example at the
quotient-septic / mixed level through invariants such as
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\Delta_7.
\]
So any viable continuation of route 2 must hybridize the repeated-source moving
shear
\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda
\]
with higher non-universal data of that kind.
\end{remark}
```

_Thought for 21s_

The next math push is to **leave route 2 as a closed subsystem** and force a contradiction by importing the **first non-universal data**, which in this draft means the quotient-septic / mixed layer.

In other words, I would stop trying to get more out of
\[
\Psi_a,\qquad \mathfrak D(a,h),\qquad \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},\qquad D_{f_a}(a,h),
\qquad f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda.
\]
You’ve now pushed that package to its ceiling. The universal-lift argument says any theorem phrased only in that language can be modeled by an arbitrary analytic normalized \(\mathcal Z\), and the explicit source model shows the delayed-crossing scenario really happens there. So the next proof step has to use something the universal model does **not** control.

That points straight at
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\Delta_7,
\]
or the mixed finite-jet package built from them.

The theorem I would attack is this:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{source-pinned septic obstruction theorem}
}
\]

Take the moving shear
\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda
\]
along the continued repeated-source critical branch
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h(a))=0.
\]
Show that if a delayed rooted crossing occurs,
\[
D_{f_a}(a,h(a))=0,
\]
then the septic invariant of \(f_a\) — equivalently the quotient-septic data seen by the corresponding normalized profile — must satisfy a forbidden sign or vanishing pattern.

That is the first place the RH branch could differ from the universal normalized models.

More concretely, I’d try to prove one of these three statements.

First choice:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0,\quad D_{f_a}(a,h)=0
\;\Longrightarrow\;
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}(f_a)] \text{ or } \Delta_7^{(f_a)}
\text{ vanishes / changes sign in a way impossible on the continued branch.}
}
\]

Second choice:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A delayed route-2 rooted crossing forces the moving shear }f_a
\text{ into one of the mixed bad low-order channels already isolated elsewhere.}
}
\]

Third choice, a bit softer but maybe easier:

\[
\boxed{
\text{On the continued route-2 branch, } [A_7^{\mathfrak f}(f_a)] \text{ has a fixed sign or nonvanishing class,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{while any rooted crossing would force the opposite sign or trivial class.}
}
\]

That is the right next move because it uses the first data that are not universally realizable by the normalized model
\[
c=1,\quad v_5=t,\quad \lambda=t^2,\quad u_5''=2\mathcal Z.
\]

So the tactical plan I’d follow is:

1. Define the septic invariant of the **source-pinned moving shear** \(f_a\) cleanly in the same gauge/quotient language the draft already uses.

2. Compute how that invariant transforms along the repeated-source critical branch. The key question is whether
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\]
simplifies the septic expression enough to make its sign or vanishing rigid.

3. Evaluate that invariant near the seeding odd zero, where the local branch is explicit. That gives the initial sign/class on the actual RH branch.

4. Show a delayed rooted crossing would force a contradictory septic pattern. If that works, route 2 closes, but only after hybridizing with higher data.

So the next push is not another sign argument inside the old package. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{hybridize route 2 with the quotient-septic / mixed package, starting with }f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda.
}
\]

That is where I would spend effort now.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 03:38:58)

_Thought for 6m 2s_

I pushed on the quotient-septic hybrid, and the clean outcome is this:

\[
\boxed{\textbf{the right next theorem is a septic bridge lemma, and } \Delta_7 \text{ alone is not enough.}}
\]

Here is why.

The moving shear is
\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\qquad m:=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
The quotient-septic geometry already in the draft lives in the affine chart
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
y(h)=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)},
\]
and for each slope \(m\) it packages affine lines by
\[
\phi_m(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)-m\,v_5(h)}{c(h)}=y(h)-m\,x(h).
\]
This is exactly the higher-order object that still remembers the moving-shear parameter \(m\).

And the draft already gives the derivative formula
\[
\phi_m'(h)=\frac{N(h)-m\,M(h)}{c(h)^2}.
\]

So:

- \(\phi_m'(h)=0\) means the affine line of slope \(m\) is tangent to the quotient-septic curve \(\Gamma(h)=(x(h),y(h))\) at \(h\);
- \(\phi_m(a)=\phi_m(h)\) means that same line also passes through the point \(\Gamma(a)\).

That is exactly the tangent-separator geometry your later ECT/adjacent-boundary theorems control.

So the first strong conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the first non-universal ingredient is not } \Delta_7 \text{ by itself, but the slope-selected family } \phi_m.
}
\]

That is already a genuine sharpening of the strategy.

Now for the actual attack.

A delayed rooted crossing on route 2 is defined by the lower-order conditions
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0,
\qquad
D_{f_a}(a,h)=0,
\qquad
m=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
The only way to bring in the quotient-septic geometry is to prove the bridge

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0,\quad D_{f_a}(a,h)=0
\Longrightarrow
\phi_m(a)=\phi_m(h),\quad \phi_m'(h)=0.
}
\]

If that lemma were true, then the repeated-source rooted point would force:

- a tangent line of slope \(m=\mathcal Z(a)\) to the quotient-septic curve \(\Gamma\) at \(h\),
- passing through the point \(\Gamma(a)\).

And that is exactly the kind of configuration the ECT/tangent-separator machine is built to kill on turning-boundary generic blocks.

So the math push reduces the hybrid route to one very concrete theorem:

\[
\boxed{\textbf{septic bridge lemma}}
\]

with the explicit target identities
\[
\phi_{\mathcal Z(a)}(a)=\phi_{\mathcal Z(a)}(h),
\qquad
\phi_{\mathcal Z(a)}'(h)=0.
\]

I do **not** think the current draft proves that yet. But I can say more about why this is the right place to focus.

First, it avoids the universality obstruction.  
The current route-2 package was universal because it only saw the normalized planar \(D_a\)-model. The family \(\phi_m\) is genuinely higher-order and depends on \(\Delta_7\), so it is the first place the quotient-septic layer can actually interact with the moving shear.

Second, it interfaces directly with the existing geometry.  
Once you have \(\phi_m(a)=\phi_m(h)\) and \(\phi_m'(h)=0\), you are no longer guessing what to do with \(\Delta_7\): you have an affine tangent-separator incidence on \(\Gamma\), and the draft already has a large machine for excluding pair-pair / tangent-line recurrences on ECT intervals and across generic turning boundaries.

Third, it isolates the real missing algebra.  
All the remaining work is to derive the higher-order analog of the lower-order rooted conditions. In plain language: show that the lower repeated-source root for \(f_a\) propagates to a line-incidence/tangency condition on the quotient-septic residual curve.

So my next attack would be very explicit:

1. Write the fixed-sector quintic and septic coefficients of the source-pinned moving shear \(f_a\) in terms of the existing one-pair data.
2. Compute the quotient-septic residual for that moving shear.
3. See whether the conditions
   \[
   D_{f_a}(a,h)=0,\qquad \partial_h D_{u_5}/D_\lambda=0
   \]
   force the equal-intercept and tangent conditions for \(\phi_m\).

If that bridge works, route 2 has a real chance of closing on the existing ECT/tangent-separator framework. If it fails, that failure itself will tell you the quotient-septic layer is still not the right non-universal input and you need an even tighter hybrid with the mixed package.

So the next push is no longer vague:

\[
\boxed{
\text{derive the septic bridge }
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0,\ D_{f_a}(a,h)=0
\Rightarrow
\phi_{\mathcal Z(a)}(a)=\phi_{\mathcal Z(a)}(h),\ \phi'_{\mathcal Z(a)}(h)=0.
}
\]

That is the attack I would do next.

_Thought for 2m 18s_

I attacked the septic bridge directly, and I think the honest result is:

\[
\boxed{\textbf{the naive septic bridge lemma is false.}}
\]

More precisely, the lower repeated-source rooted conditions
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0,
\qquad

\qquad

\[

\qquad

\qquad
\phi_m(t):=\frac{\Delta_7(t)-m v_5(t)}{c(t)}.
\]

And this failure already occurs in a genuine analytic source model with completely generic quotient-septic geometry.

---

## 1) Reuse the existing route-2 source countermodel

Take the normalized source model
\[
c(t)=1,\qquad v_5(t)=t,\qquad \lambda(t)=t^2,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal R(t)=t(t-1)(t^2-4t-2)
=t^4-5t^3+2t^2+2t,
\]
\[
\mathcal Z(t)=\int_0^t \mathcal R(u)\,du
=
\frac15 t^5-\frac54 t^4+\frac23 t^3+t^2.
\]
Choose \(u_5\) so that
\[
u_5''(t)=2\mathcal Z(t).
\]

Then
\[
x=t,\qquad S=t^2,\qquad \Psi_a(h)=D_a(h),
\]
and the source critical equation is exactly
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\iff
\partial_h D_a(h)=0.
\]

As in the earlier attack, this model has a delayed rooted point on the continued born branch at
\[
a_*\approx -0.5805673462,
\qquad
h_*\approx 0.3888336023,
\]
with
\[
\mathfrak D(a_*,h_*)=0,
\qquad
D_{f_{a_*}}(a_*,h_*)=0,
\qquad
m_*:=\mathcal Z(a_*)\approx 0.0513997351.
\]

So this is already a genuine source-level rooted crossing for the lower route-2 package.

---

## 2) Now choose perfectly good quotient-septic data

Set
\[
u_7(t):=t,\qquad v_7(t):=0.
\]
Then
\[
\Delta_7(t)=u_7(t)v_5(t)-u_5(t)v_7(t)=t^2.
\]

This is analytic, and with \(c=1,\ v_5=t\) one gets
\[
x(t)=\frac{v_5(t)}{c(t)}=t,
\qquad
y(t)=\frac{\Delta_7(t)}{c(t)}=t^2.
\]

So the quotient-septic curve is simply
\[
\Gamma(t)=(t,t^2),
\]
which is as generic as one could want:
\[
M(t)=c v_5'-c'v_5=1,
\qquad
N(t)=c\Delta_7'-c'\Delta_7=2t,
\qquad
W(t)=2.
\]
Hence
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad W\neq 0
\]
everywhere. So this lies on a perfectly good ECT / convex quotient-septic block.

For the slope
\[
m_*= \mathcal Z(a_*),
\]
the slope-selected quotient-septic function is
\[
\phi_{m_*}(t)=y(t)-m_*x(t)=t^2-m_* t.
\]

---

## 3) The bridge conclusion fails at the rooted point

The derivative condition would require
\[
\phi_{m_*}'(h_*)=0.
\]
But
\[
\phi_{m_*}'(t)=2t-m_*,
\]
so
\[
\phi_{m_*}'(h_*)=2h_*-m_*
\approx 2(0.3888336023)-0.0513997351
\approx 0.7262674695\neq 0.
\]

So the tangent condition already fails.

The equal-intercept condition would require
\[
\phi_{m_*}(a_*)=\phi_{m_*}(h_*).
\]
But
\[
\phi_{m_*}(a_*)-\phi_{m_*}(h_*)
=
(a_*-h_*)(a_*+h_*-m_*),
\]
and numerically
\[
a_*-h_*\approx -0.9694009485,
\qquad
a_*+h_*-m_*\approx -0.2431334789,
\]
so
\[
\phi_{m_*}(a_*)-\phi_{m_*}(h_*)\approx 0.2356938251\neq 0.
\]

So the secant/incidence condition fails as well.

Thus at a genuine delayed rooted crossing of the lower route-2 package, the quotient-septic line of slope \(m_*\) need be neither tangent at \(h_*\) nor incident through \(\Gamma(a_*)\).

---

## 4) Conclusion

This gives a clean no-go theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Lower route-2 rootedness does not imply the quotient-septic tangent/separator configuration.}
}
\]

Even under:

- a genuine analytic source model,
- a genuine delayed rooted crossing,
- and a completely generic quotient-septic block
  \[
  c\neq 0,\quad M\neq 0,\quad W\neq 0,
  \]
the naive bridge
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0,\quad D_{f_a}(a,h)=0
\Longrightarrow
\phi_{\mathcal Z(a)}(a)=\phi_{\mathcal Z(a)}(h),\ 
\phi'_{\mathcal Z(a)}(h)=0
\]
fails.

So the septic layer does **not** automatically couple to route 2 in the hoped-for way.

---

## 5) What this means for the next attack

This is actually useful, because it tells you exactly what kind of hybrid theorem is still possible.

A successful septic/mixed hybrid cannot be of the simple form:

> lower rootedness \(\Rightarrow\) quotient-septic tangent separator.

That statement is false.

So the next live theorem has to use **additional higher constraints on the actual RH branch**, not just the existence of a rooted point in the lower package.

In practice, that means something like:

- rootedness **plus** a condition on \([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\),
- or rootedness **plus** a mixed bad-channel condition,
- or a theorem saying that on the actual RH branch the particular \(\Delta_7\) arising from the canonical septic package is not free in the way it is in the counterexample.

So the next math push is now much sharper:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{look for the first theorem that constrains } \Delta_7
\text{ relative to the lower route-2 data,}
}
\]
not a theorem that tries to derive quotient-septic tangency from rootedness alone.

That is the clean next attack.

Here is the strongest clean push I can get now.

The **provenance-sensitive order-7 layer** really does collapse to a single scalar graph problem.

That is useful, because it tells you exactly what theorem is missing.

Let
\[
\mu:=\frac{c}{v_5},\qquad
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
\phi:=\lambda^{[1]}
\]
on the region \(v_5\neq 0\), where \([\,\cdot\,]^{[1]}\) is the direct highest-new \(q^{(7)}\)-slice. By the draft’s weight-one reduction,
\[
\Delta_7^{[1]}=v_5\,\phi.
\]

From this alone, you can compute the whole direct-slice quotient-septic geometry.

First,
\[
\lambda^{[1]}=\phi.
\]

Next,
\[
L:=v_5\Delta_7'-v_5'\Delta_7
\]
has weight-one part
\[
L^{[1]}
=
v_5(v_5\phi)' - v_5'(v_5\phi)
=
v_5^2\phi'.
\]

\[
\mu'=\left(\frac{c}{v_5}\right)'=-\frac{M}{v_5^2},
\]
the dual slope variable
\[
\beta:=\frac{d\lambda}{d\mu}=-\frac{L}{M}
\]
has weight-one part
\[
\boxed{
\beta^{[1]}=\frac{d\phi}{d\mu}.
}
\]

Likewise the intercept variable
\[
m:=\lambda-\mu\beta=\frac{N}{M}
\]
has weight-one part
\[
\boxed{
m^{[1]}=\phi-\mu\frac{d\phi}{d\mu}.
}
\]

So on the direct highest-new slice, the dual tangent-line curve is exactly the ordinary dual tangent-line curve of the scalar graph
\[
y=\phi(\mu).
\]

That is the first real structural theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{direct weight-one quotient-septic geometry = tangent-line geometry of the scalar graph }y=\phi(\mu).
}
\]

You can push one step further.

From the draft’s identity
\[
\beta'=-\frac{v_5W}{M^2},
\]
divide by \(\mu'=-M/v_5^2\) to get
\[
\frac{d\beta}{d\mu}=\frac{v_5^3}{M^3}W.
\]
Taking weight-one parts gives
\[
\boxed{
\phi_{\mu\mu}
=
\frac{v_5^3}{M^3}W^{[1]},
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
W^{[1]}=\frac{M^3}{v_5^3}\phi_{\mu\mu}.
}
\]

So the weight-one ECT / convexity question for \((c,v_5,\Delta_7)\) is exactly the convexity question for \(\phi\).

This is, I think, the right new reduction.

It means the next provenance-sensitive attack is no longer vague “use \([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\) somehow.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{prove a convexity / ECT theorem for the direct scalar }\phi(\mu).
}
\]

In practical terms, any one of these would be enough to really move things:

\[
\phi_{\mu\mu}\ \text{has one sign on the relevant block},
\]
or more weakly
\[
(1,\mu,\phi)\ \text{is an ECT-system on the relevant block},
\]
or even more weakly
\[
\text{the graph }y=\phi(\mu)\text{ has no pair-pair secant/tangent recurrence compatible with the route-2 branch.}

This also explains why the previous “arbitrary \(\Delta_7\)” attacks were too loose: arbitrary \(\Delta_7\) is too free, but the direct provenance slice is not arbitrary geometry anymore — it is encoded by a single scalar \(\phi\), and the whole line-incidence problem becomes classical graph geometry.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 04:13:21)

I’m checking the exact direct-slice formula and surrounding order-7 identities in the draft so I can push on \(\phi_{\mu\mu}\) concretely rather than hand-waving about convexity.

_Thought for 1m 35s_

Yes. I think there is a real new reduction here.

The global line-incidence problem on the direct weight-one slice collapses to a **two-inflection obstruction** for the scalar graph
\[
y=\phi(\mu).
\]

That is stronger and cleaner than the earlier vague “no re-entry of slope” formulation.

---

### 1. Bitangent / four-secant recurrence forces two zeros of \(\phi_{\mu\mu}\)

Let
\[
g(\mu):=\phi(\mu)-(s\mu+b).
\]

If a line \(y=s\mu+b\) is tangent to the graph \(y=\phi(\mu)\) at two distinct points
\[
\mu_1<\mu_2,
\]
then
\[
g(\mu_1)=g'(\mu_1)=0,
\qquad
g(\mu_2)=g'(\mu_2)=0.
\]
By Rolle on \(g'\), there is \(\xi\in(\mu_1,\mu_2)\) with
\[
g''(\xi)=\phi_{\mu\mu}(\xi)=0.
\]
But because \(g'\) vanishes at both endpoints and also has at least one interior zero, applying Rolle separately on \((\mu_1,\xi)\) and \((\xi,\mu_2)\) gives **two** points
\[
\xi_1,\xi_2\in(\mu_1,\mu_2),\qquad \xi_1<\xi_2,
\]
such that
\[
\phi_{\mu\mu}(\xi_1)=\phi_{\mu\mu}(\xi_2)=0.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a bitangent line for } \phi \text{ forces at least two zeros of } \phi_{\mu\mu}.
}
\]

Exactly the same proof works for a four-secant line. If
\[
g(\mu_1)=g(\mu_2)=g(\mu_3)=g(\mu_4)=0
\qquad
(\mu_1<\mu_2<\mu_3<\mu_4),
\]
then Rolle gives three zeros of \(g'\), hence at least two zeros of \(g''=\phi_{\mu\mu}\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{any }2+2\text{ secant recurrence on the graph }y=\phi(\mu)
\text{ forces at least two zeros of }\phi_{\mu\mu}.
}
\]

---

### 2. Dual-curve vertical re-entry also forces two zeros of \(\phi_{\mu\mu}\)

On the direct slice,
\[
\beta^{[1]}=\phi_\mu.
\]
So if the slope value reappears on nonadjacent branches, meaning
\[
\phi_\mu(\mu_1)=\phi_\mu(\mu_2)=\phi_\mu(\mu_3)
\qquad
(\mu_1<\mu_2<\mu_3),
\]
then Rolle applied to \(\phi_\mu\) gives at least two points
\[
\xi_1\in(\mu_1,\mu_2),\qquad \xi_2\in(\mu_2,\mu_3)
\]
with
\[
\phi_{\mu\mu}(\xi_1)=\phi_{\mu\mu}(\xi_2)=0.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{nonadjacent slope re-entry for } \phi_\mu
\text{ forces at least two zeros of }\phi_{\mu\mu}.
}
\]

Since you already proved
\[
\phi_{\mu\mu}=\frac{v_5^3}{M^3}W^{[1]},
\]
this is equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{any nonadjacent slope re-entry or pair-pair line recurrence on the direct slice
forces at least two zeros of }W^{[1]}.
}
\]

That is the new precise bottleneck.

---

### 3. Why this is genuinely useful

This sharpens the global propagation problem a lot.

You no longer need to rule out all possible secant/tangent recurrences directly.

It is enough to prove:

\[
\boxed{
W^{[1]} \text{ has at most one zero on the relevant direct-slice block.}
}
\]

Or even slightly weaker:

\[
\boxed{
\phi_{\mu\mu} \text{ does not vanish at two separated points on that block.}
}
\]

Because then:

- no nonadjacent slope re-entry of \(\phi_\mu\),
- no vertical-line re-entry on the dual direct-slice curve,
- no bitangent line to \(y=\phi(\mu)\),
- no four-secant line across two nonadjacent ECT intervals.

So the remaining endgame on the direct slice reduces to a **two-zero exclusion theorem for \(W^{[1]}\)**.

That is a much more concrete target than “global nonrecurrence.”

---

### 4. This also meshes perfectly with what the draft already knows

You already have:

- finite-order \(W=0\) local sterility,
- generic turning-boundary local exclusion,
- and the warning that naive local convexity or sign arguments are not enough globally.

The new point is:

those local results already control what happens at a **single** zero of \(W^{[1]}\).

So any remaining global recurrence must come from **two separated zeros** of \(W^{[1]}\).

That is the right way to splice the local theory into the global theorem.

In short:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local theory reduces the global direct-slice problem to proving that }W^{[1]}
\text{ cannot have two separated zeros.}
}
\]

---

### 5. The next attack after this

The next thing I would attack is therefore not general line geometry, but the explicit direct-slice formula for
\[
\phi
=
\kappa\Bigl(
(x_2-x_1)\nu_6^{(q^{(7)})}
+
v(\gamma_5-\alpha_5)^{(q^{(7)})}
\Bigr),
\]
with the aim of showing that
\[
\phi_{\mu\mu}
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
W^{[1]}
\]
has at most one zero on a relevant component.

Even something like
\[
W^{[1]} \text{ is monotone,}
\]
or
\[
W^{[1]} \text{ changes sign at most once,}
\]
would now be enough to close the direct-slice global propagation theorem.

So the real next theorem target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{two-zero exclusion for }W^{[1]} \text{ on a generic direct-slice block.}
}
\]

That is where I would push next.

_Thought for 3m 44s_

Here is the cleanest further push I can get.

The global direct-slice problem reduces to an **ordered slope-window problem**. That is stronger and more usable than the earlier “two separated zeros of \(W^{[1]}\)” phrasing.

Let
\[
\phi=\lambda^{[1]},\qquad
\beta^{[1]}=\phi_\mu,\qquad
\phi_{\mu\mu}=\frac{v_5^3}{M^3}W^{[1]}
\]
on the region where \(v_5M\neq 0\).

Write
\[
\Omega:=\{h:\ v_5(h)M(h)W^{[1]}(h)\neq 0\}.
\]
Let \(J_\alpha\) be a connected component of \(\Omega\). On \(J_\alpha\), the sign of
\[
\frac{v_5^3}{M^3}W^{[1]}
\]
is constant, so \(\phi_{\mu\mu}\) has fixed sign, hence
\[
\phi_\mu
\]
is strictly monotone there.

So each component \(J_\alpha\) carries a well-defined **slope window**
\[
I_\alpha:=\phi_\mu(J_\alpha)\subset\mathbf R.
\]

That gives the first theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Regular-component monotonicity.}
\quad
\text{On each regular direct-slice component }J_\alpha,\ \phi_\mu
\text{ is strictly monotone, so }I_\alpha
\text{ is an interval.}
}
\]

Now look at the boundaries between these components.

If \(h_b\) is an isolated finite-order zero of \(W^{[1]}\) with \(M(h_b)\neq 0\), then by the direct-slice version of the curvature formula,
\[
\phi_{\mu\mu}(h_b)=0,
\qquad
\phi_{\mu\mu\mu}(h_b)
=
-\frac{v_5(h_b)^5}{M(h_b)^4}\,(W^{[1]})'(h_b).
\]
So when \((W^{[1]})'(h_b)\neq 0\), the slope function \(\phi_\mu\) has an ordinary strict extremum there. Hence the two adjacent slope windows meet in exactly one endpoint value and are otherwise disjoint.

If \(h_b\) is a generic turning boundary \(M(h_b)=0\), then the dual asymptote theorem gives
\[
\beta=-\frac{L}{M}\to \pm\infty
\]
on both adjacent arcs, so the corresponding slope windows meet only at infinity.

So the local picture is completely rigid:

- adjacent windows can only touch at a single extremal endpoint, or at infinity across a turning boundary;
- all genuinely dangerous overlap must be **nonadjacent**.

That gives the second theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Slope-window reduction.}
\quad
\text{The remaining global direct-slice problem is exactly to prove}
\quad
I_\alpha\cap I_\beta=\varnothing
\quad\text{for nonadjacent same-parity components.}
}
\]

This packages the whole endgame very cleanly, because the equivalent formulations in the draft now become:

- no nonadjacent pair-pair line on the primal quotient-septic curve;
- no nonadjacent same-parity vertical-line re-entry for the dual curve \(T\);
- no nonadjacent slope re-entry for \(\phi_\mu\);

and all three are the same as **disjointness of nonadjacent slope windows**.

It also sharpens the earlier inflection obstruction. If
\[
I_\alpha\cap I_\beta\neq\varnothing
\qquad(\alpha<\beta,\ \beta\ge \alpha+2),
\]
then some slope value is attained on both components, so by Rolle \(\phi_{\mu\mu}\) must vanish at least once between successive returns; hence between the two components there are at least two zeros of \(W^{[1]}\). But the window formulation is stronger: it tells you the exact global datum to control is not merely “how many zeros,” but the **ordering of the image intervals**
\[
I_\alpha=\phi_\mu(J_\alpha).
\]

So the next real theorem target is now:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{window-order theorem for }\phi_\mu.
}
\]

For example, any one of the following would close the direct-slice propagation problem:

\[
\sup I_\alpha < \inf I_{\alpha+2}
\quad\text{for all relevant }\alpha,
\]
or the reverse ordering, or any monotone nesting law that keeps same-parity windows disjoint.

That is a better target than “prove \(W^{[1]}\) has one sign,” because it is exactly what the existing local theory plus the direct-slice formulas reduce the global problem to.

So the next attack I would make is:

- compute the endpoint values of \(I_\alpha\) at isolated \(W^{[1]}=0\) boundaries and at generic turning boundaries using the explicit direct-slice formula for \(\phi\),
- then try to prove a monotone ordering of these endpoint values across components.

That is the cleanest mathematical push from where the draft stands now.
## User (2026-04-21 04:27:20)
